Critique of Claim Classification: From 36 to 512 Cases
Presents and critiques a classification of two-claimant cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the original and revised classifications of two-claimant cases and explain how the inclusion of claim type, evidence, hand, and dating yields 512 possible scenarios.

Core Idea
Exhaustive classification of claim cases requires multiplying claim type, evidence, hand, and dating, yielding 512 possibilities.

In this passage, the commentator of al-Bahr al-Rā’iq critiques a classification from al-‘Imādiyya that enumerated 36 cases when two men claim the same property. He argues it is not comprehensive and proposes a more refined classification that expands to 512 cases by considering nine claim types, four evidence scenarios, four hand positions, and four dating possibilities. This refinement underscores the complexity of evidentiary conflicts in Hanafi law and the systematic approach of its jurists.

Guided Path
1
Understand the original classification
Identify the three categories of claim (absolute ownership, inheritance, purchase), three positions of the property (in a third party's hand, in both hands, in one of the claimants' hands), and four dating scenarios (no date, same date, one earlier, one dates other does not). Multiply: 3 × 3 × 4 = 36.
2
Identify the critique
The author states 'ليس بحاصر' (not comprehensive). He then provides a more detailed breakdown starting with nine claim types based on the nature of ownership (absolute vs. by a cause, repeatable vs. non-repeatable, equal vs. stronger, etc.).
The nine types are derived from combinations of ownership basis and mutability.
3
Follow the new classification arithmetic
9 claim types × 4 evidence scenarios (both prove, only one proves, none with no preference, one with preference) = 32. Then 32 × 4 hand positions (third party, both hands, hand of one claimant? The text says three but counts four) = 128. Then 128 × 4 dating scenarios = 512.
The text explicitly gives 128 and then 512, though the hand position count is ambiguous.
4
Appreciate the significance
The refined classification shows that Hanafi jurists systematically considered many factors in claim cases. Al-Ramli encourages reflection, indicating its practical utility in court.
Understanding this classification helps in analyzing actual claim disputes in Hanafi courts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أنه قال في العمادية : اعلم أن الرجلين إذا ادعيا عيناً وبرهنا فلا يخلو إما أن يدعيا ملكاً مطلقاً أو إرثاً أو شراء، وكل قسم على ثلاثة إما أن يكون المدعي في يد ثالث أو في يدهما أو في يد أحدهما، وكل وجه على أربعة أقسام لأنه إما أن لا يؤرخا أو أرخا تاريخاً واحداً أو أرخا وتاريخ أحدهما أسبق أو أرخ أحدهما لا الآخر وجملة ذلك ستة وثلاثون أقول : إن هذا التقسيم ليس بحاصر والصواب أن يقال : إذا ادعيا عيناً فإما أن يدعيا ملكاً مطلقاً أو ملكاً . ا بسبب متحد قابل للتكرار أو غير قابل له، أو مختلف أحدهما أقوى من الآخر، أو مستويان من واحد أو من متعدد، أو يدعي أحدهما الملك المطلق والآخر الملك بسبب، أو أحدهما ما يتكرر والآخر ما لا يتكرر فهي تسعة. وكل منهما إما أن يبرهن أو يبرهن أحدهما فقط، أو لا برهان لواحد منهما ولا مرجح أو لأحدهما مرجح فهي أربعة صارت اثنين وثلاثين. وكل منها إما أن يكون المدعي في يد ثالث أو في يدهما أو في يد أحدهما فهي أربعة فصلاً ا هـ. سيذكره المصنف في هذا الباب قوله : (ثم بعده إذا أقام صاحب اليد البينة أنه ملكه لا يقبل) انظر ما كتبناه عند قوله وقضى له إن نكل مرة . قوله : (أقول أن هذا التقسيم ليس بحاصر والصواب أن يقال الخ) قال الرملي: تأمل في هذا التقسيم يظهر لك ما فيه . صارت مائة وثمانية وعشرين وكل منها على أربعة أما إذا لم يؤرخا أو أرخا واستويا أو سبق أحدهما أو أرخ أحدهما صارت خمسمائة واثنى عشر . كذا وهو
Then know that he said in al-'Imadiyya: Know that when two men claim an object and provide evidence, it is not free from either both claiming absolute ownership, or inheritance, or purchase. And each category is of three types: either the claimant is in the hand of a third party, or in their both hands, or in the hand of one of them. And each aspect has four divisions: either they do not date, or they date with one date, or they date and the date of one is earlier, or one dates and the other does not. Total: thirty-six. I say: This classification is not comprehensive. The correct is to say: When two men claim an object, either they claim absolute ownership, or ownership by a single cause that can be repeated or not, or different causes with one stronger, or equal from one or multiple, or one claims absolute ownership and the other ownership by cause, or one claims what can be repeated and the other what cannot. That is nine. Each of these has either both prove, or only one proves, or no proof for either with no preference, or one has a preference. That is four, making thirty-two. Each of these has either the claimant in the hand of a third, or in their both hands, or in the hand of one. That is four. End of section. The author will mention in this chapter his statement: (Then after that, if the possessor of the hand brings evidence that it is his property, it is not accepted). Look at what we wrote at his statement 'and judgment is given to him if he refuses once'. His statement: (I say this classification is not comprehensive and the correct is to say...). Al-Ramli said: Reflect on this classification, it will become clear to you what is in it. It becomes one hundred and twenty-eight, and each of these has four: either they do not date, or they date and are equal, or one precedes, or one dates. It becomes five hundred and twelve. This and it.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a methodological discussion on classifying the cases that arise when two men claim the same property (ayn) and both provide evidence. The author quotes from al-'Imadiyya a classification that yields 36 cases based on type of claim (ownership, inheritance, purchase), position of the property relative to the claimants (in third party's hand, in both their hands, or in one's hand), and dating of evidence. The author (the commentator of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) criticizes this as not comprehensive (laysa bi-hasir) and offers his own classification that first distinguishes nine types of claims (e.g., absolute ownership vs. ownership by a cause, single cause that can be repeated vs. not, etc.), then adds four possibilities of evidence (both prove, one proves, none with preference, one with preference) resulting in 32, then four possibilities of hand position making 128, and finally four possibilities of dating making 512 cases. This refinement shows the complexity of claim litigation in Hanafi law. The passage also refers to the earlier ruling on evidence after judgment and includes a remark by al-Ramli encouraging reflection on this classification.

Key Terms
تقسيم (taqsīm): Classification of legal cases for analysis.
تاريخ (tārīkh): The date affixed to evidence (bayyina) to show precedence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, how many total cases result from the author's revised classification?
A) 36
B) 128
C) 512
D) 576

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi approach to classifying claim cases is exhaustive, considering multiple variables to ensure no scenario is overlooked.

Day of Death vs. Day of Killing in Judicial Testimony
Explains the rule and its branches from multiple Hanafi sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule distinguishing the day of death from the day of killing in judicial testimony and apply it to marriage and contract branches.

Core Idea
Day of death is inconclusive; day of killing is definitive for judicial precedence.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between natural death and killing when evaluating conflicting testimonies about dates. This rule has practical branches for inheritance, marriage, and other contracts. We will unpack the rule from the major Hanafi texts and see how it resolves apparent contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule and Its Source
State the rule: the day of death does not enter under judicial consideration, but the day of killing does. Note that this is found in multiple authoritative Hanafi sources (al-Imadiyyah, al-Zahiriyyah, etc.).
The rule is about accepting testimony when dates conflict – death is taken as uncertain, killing as certain.
2
Apply the Rule to Branches
Work through the branches from al-Bazzaziyyah: (1) If an heir proves death on day X, and a woman proves marriage after X, the marriage is upheld. (2) If an heir proves killing on day Y, and a woman proves marriage after Y, the marriage is not accepted.
For contracts and debts, the same logic applies: killing precludes later acts; death does not.
3
Analyze the Analogy from al-Walwalji
Consider the analogy: a woman proves the man was in Mecca on the day of sacrifice; another proves marriage on the same day in Khurasan. The second is rejected because the first is conclusive. Similarly, marriage after killing is impossible.
Both marriage and killing enter judicial consideration, so their dates are definitive.
4
Examine the Inheritance Case from al-Zahiriyyah
Explore the case where a claim of inheritance involves conflicting death dates. Some scholars accept the defense that the woman died before the man, based on the rule that day of death does not enter consideration; others reject it.
This shows that the rule is not absolute – there is difference of opinion among scholars.
5
Understand the Scope and Limits
The rule applies when testimony about the day of death or killing is used to establish precedence over other events. It does not apply when death is widely known (mustafid) – then the judge relies on certainty, not the rule.
Al-Ramli clarifies that if death is common knowledge, the rule is not invoked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن يوم الموت لا يدخل تحت القضاء ويوم القتل يدخل هكذا في العمادية والظهيرية والولوالجية والبزازية وغيرها. وفرعوا على الأول ما لو برهن الوارث على موت مورثه في يوم ثم برهنت امرأة على أن مورثه كان نكحها بعد ذلك اليوم يقضى لها بالنكاح، وعلى الثاني لو برهن الوارث على أنه قتل يوم كذا فبرهنت المرأة على أن هذا المقتول نكحها بعد ذلك اليوم لا يقبل، وعلى هذا جميع العقود والمداينات وكذا لو برهن الوارث على أن مورثه قتل يوم كذا فبرهن المدعى عليه أنه مات قبل هذا بزمان لا يسمع، ولو برهن على أن مورثه قتل يوم كذا فبرهن المدعى عليه أنه قتله فلان قبل هذا بزمان يكون دفعاً لدخوله تحت القضاء؛ هذه عبارة البزازية. وزاد الولوالجي موضحاً للثانية بقوله : ألا ترى أن امرأة لو أقامت البينة أنه يوم النحر بمكة فقضى بشهودها ثم أقامت أخرى بينة أنه تزوجها يوم النحر بخراسان لا تقبل بينة المرأة الأخرى لأن النكاح يدخل تحت القضاء فاعتبر ذلك التاريخ، فإذا ادعت امرأة أخرى بعد ذلك التاريخ بتاريخ لم يقبل ا هـ . قوله : (وزاد الولوالجي) قال الرملي أي في كتاب القضاء في أواخر الفصل الرابع : وقوله موضحاً للثانية» يعني دعوى المرأة النكاح بعد ثبوت القتل في يوم كذا قوله: (فإذا ادعت امرأة أخرى بعد ذلك التاريخ الخ قال الرملي وجه الشبه بين المسألتين أن تاريخ برهان المرأة على نكاح المقتول مخالف لتاريخ القتل إذ لا يتصور بعد قتله أن ينكح كما أن نكاح الثانية له يوم النحر بخراسان لا يتصور مع نكاح الأولى له يومه بمكه فهو مخالف من هذه الحيثية فأشبهت هذه المسألة الأولى في المخالفة، وكل من النكاح والقتل يدخل تحت الحكم فتأمل. وفي الظهيرية ادعى ضيعة في يد رجل أنها كانت لفلان مات وتركها ميراثاً لفلانة لا وارث له غيرها، ثم إن فلانة ماتت وتركتها ميراثاً لي لا وارث لها غيري وقضى القاضي له بالضيعة فقال المقضي عليه دفعاً للدعوى إن فلانة التي تدعي أنت الإرث عنها لنفسك ماتت قبل فلان الذي تدعي الإرث عنه لفلانة اختلفوا فيه بعضهم قالوا إنه صحيح وبعضهم قالوا : إنه غير صحيح بناء على أن يوم الموت لا يدخل تحت القضاء ا.هـ. قوله : (وفي الظهيرية ادعى ضيعة في يد رجل الخ) قال الرملي : إذا كان الموت مستفيضاً علم به كل صغير وكبير وكل عالم وجاهل لا يقضى له ولا يكون بطريق أن القاضي قبل البينة على ذلك الموت بل يكون بطريق التيقن بكذب المدعي ؛ ارجع إلى التتارخانية من كتاب الشهادة في الفصل الثامن عشر يظهر لك صحة ما قلته . وفيها قبله بعد ما ذكر الفرق بين يوم الموت ويوم القتل قال : غير أن مسألة أخرى ترد إشكالاً على هذا وهي أن الرجل إذا ادعى على رجل أنه قتل أباه عمداً بالسيف منذ عشرين سنة وأنه وارثه لا وارث له سواه وأقام البينة على ذلك فجاءت امرأة ومعها ولد وأقامت البينة أن والد هذا تزوجها منذ خمسة عشر سنة وأن هذا ولده منها ووارثه مع ابنه هذا قال أبو حنيفة : أستحسن في هذ أن أجيز بينة المرأة وأثبت نسب الولد ولا أبطل بينة الابن على القتل. وكان هذا الاستحسان للاحتياط في أمر النسب بدليل أنها لو أقامت البينة على النكاح ولم تأت بالولد فالبينة بينة الابن وله الميراث دون المرأة، وهذا قول أبي يوسف ومحمد ا هـ . فقد علمت مما في الظهيرية استثناء مسألة من قولهم يوم الموت لا يدخل تحت القضاء على قول البعض واستثناء مسألة من قولهم يوم القتل يدخل فافهم. قوله : (ولا أبطل بينة الابن على القتل) قال الرملي الظاهر أن حرف النفي زائد ولم يذكره في التتارخانية وعبارته : ولو أقام رجل البينة أن هذا الرجل قتل أباه منذ عشرين سنة، وأقامت المرأة البينة أنه تزوجها منذ خمس عشرة سنة وأن هؤلاء أولاده منها ؛ استحسن أبو حنيفة رحمه الله إن أجاز بينة المرأة وأثبت النسب وأبطل بينة الابن على القتل والقياس أن يقضى ببينة القتل .اهـ.
Then know that the day of death does not enter under judicial consideration, and the day of killing enters; this is found in al-Imadiyyah, al-Zahiriyyah, al-Walwaljiyyah, al-Bazzaziyyah, and others. And they derived from the first: if the heir proves the death of his testator on a certain day, then a woman proves that the testator married her after that day, she is judged to have the marriage. And from the second: if the heir proves that he was killed on a certain day, then a woman proves that this killed person married her after that day, it is not accepted. And similarly for all contracts and debts. Likewise, if the heir proves that his testator was killed on a certain day, and the defendant proves that he died before this time, it is not heard. And if he proves that his testator was killed on a certain day, and the defendant proves that someone else killed him before this time, it is a repulsion of its entering under judicial consideration. This is the wording of al-Bazzaziyyah. And al-Walwalji added clarifying the second saying: Do you not see that if a woman presents evidence that he was on the day of sacrifice in Mecca, and judgment is given on her witnesses, then another presents evidence that he married her on the day of sacrifice in Khurasan, the evidence of the other woman is not accepted because marriage enters under judicial consideration and that date is considered. So if another woman claims after that date with a later date, it is not accepted. End quote. His saying: (And al-Walwalji added) al-Ramli said: i.e., in the book of judicial rulings at the end of the fourth chapter: and his saying 'clarifying the second' means the woman's claim of marriage after the establishment of the killing on a certain day. His saying: (if another woman claims after that date, etc.) al-Ramli said: the similarity between the two issues is that the date of the woman's evidence of marriage of the killed person contradicts the date of killing, since after his death it is inconceivable that he married, just as the marriage of the second to him on the day of sacrifice in Khurasan is inconceivable with the marriage of the first to him on the same day in Mecca, so it is contradictory in this respect, and this issue resembles the first in contradiction, and both marriage and killing enter under judgment, so consider. His saying: (And in al-Zahiriyyah: a claim of a property in the hand of a man...) al-Ramli said: If death is widely known, known to every young and old, every scholar and ignorant, it is not judged, and it is not by way of the judge accepting evidence on that death, but rather by way of certainty of the plaintiff's lying; refer to al-Tatar-Khaniyyah from the book of testimony in the eighteenth chapter, the correctness of what I said will appear to you. And in it before that, after mentioning the difference between the day of death and the day of killing, he said: However, another issue raises a problem on this, and it is that if a man claims against a man that he killed his father intentionally with a sword twenty years ago, and that he is his heir with no other heir, and he presents evidence on that, then a woman comes with a child and presents evidence that this man's father married her fifteen years ago and that this is his child from her and he is his heir along with his son; Abu Hanifa said: I use istihsan in this to accept the woman's evidence and establish the lineage of the child, and I do not nullify the son's evidence on the killing. And this istihsan was for caution in the matter of lineage, evidenced by the fact that if she presented evidence on the marriage and did not bring a child, then the evidence is the son's and he has the inheritance without the woman. And this is the statement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. End quote. So you know from what is in al-Zahiriyyah the exception of one issue from their statement that the day of death does not enter under judicial consideration according to some, and the exception of one issue from their statement that the day of killing enters, so understand. His saying: (And I do not nullify the son's evidence on the killing) al-Ramli said: Apparently the negation particle is extra, and he did not mention it in al-Tatar-Khaniyyah, and his wording: If a man presents evidence that this man killed his father twenty years ago, and a woman presents evidence that he married her fifteen years ago and that these are his children from her; Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, used istihsan to accept the woman's evidence and establish the lineage and he nullified the son's evidence on the killing, and by analogy the judgment would be given on the evidence of killing. End quote.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explaining the distinction between the day of death and the day of killing regarding judicial acceptance of testimony. The rule is that the day of death does not 'enter under judicial consideration,' meaning that if testimony about the day of death contradicts other established facts (e.g., a marriage after that day), it is not accepted. Conversely, the day of killing does enter, so testimony about the day of killing is accepted as long as it does not conflict with subsequent events. The commentator presents branches from al-Bazzaziyyah: if an heir proves death on a day, and a woman proves marriage after that day, the marriage is upheld; if an heir proves killing on a day, and a woman proves marriage after that day, the marriage is not accepted because killing is taken as definitive. Al-Walwalji clarifies with an analogy: if a woman proves the man was in Mecca on the day of sacrifice, and another proves marriage on the same day in Khurasan, the second is rejected because the first is conclusive. Al-Ramli explains the similarity. The passage then presents a case from al-Zahiriyyah involving conflicting death dates in an inheritance dispute; some scholars accept the defense based on the rule, others reject it. A second case from al-Zahiriyyah involves an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa uses istihsan to accept a woman's evidence establishing lineage over a son's evidence of a killing, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad follow qiyas (analogy) and would give precedence to the son's evidence. The text notes that caution in lineage justifies the istihsan, and Abu Hanifa does not nullify the son's evidence. Al-Ramli clarifies that in some reports, Abu Hanifa does nullify the son's evidence, meaning the negation in the text may be a scribal error. The overall lesson shows exceptions to the general rule.

Key Terms
يوم الموت (yawm al-mawt): The specific day of a person's death; in judicial testimony, this day is not considered conclusive for precluding later events.
يوم القتل (yawm al-qatl): The specific day a person was killed; in judicial testimony, this day is taken as definitive and precludes later events.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to override qiyas for equity, here used to protect lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An heir proves that the deceased was killed on January 1. The defendant then proves that the deceased actually died from natural causes on January 2. What is the ruling?
A) The defendant's evidence is accepted because the day of killing does not enter judicial consideration.
B) The defendant's evidence is not heard because the day of killing is definitive.
C) Both evidence are accepted and the judge decides based on preponderance.
D) The defendant's evidence is rejected because it contradicts the heir's.

Key Takeaway
The day of killing is judicially definitive, while the day of death is not, leading to acceptance of later events after death but rejection after killing.

10 min
Istihsan for Lineage: Abu Hanifa's Exception to the Day of Killing Rule
Explains Abu Hanifa's istihsan exception to the day of killing rule for lineage, and the disagreement with the Sahibayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Hanifa's use of istihsan to prioritize lineage over the day of killing rule and evaluate the opposing view of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas: lineage is too precious to be nullified by a rule.

The general rule states that the day of killing is definitive. However, Abu Hanifa makes an exception when a woman's lineage claim conflicts with a son's killing testimony. This shows that substantive values, such as preserving lineage, can override procedural rules through istihsan. We will examine the case and the disagreement with the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Conflicting Claims
A son claims that his father was killed 20 years ago (proves killing). A woman claims that the same man married her 15 years ago and bore a child. The marriage is after the killing—so normally the killing rule would reject it.
The woman's evidence is about a later event after the killing.
2
Identify the Qiyas (Analogy) Position
By qiyas, the son's evidence on killing should be preferred, and the woman's evidence rejected. This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn).
They strictly apply the day of killing rule.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's Istihsan
Abu Hanifa uses istihsan to accept the woman's evidence, establish lineage, and not nullify the son's evidence on killing. The rationale is caution in lineage (al-ihtiyat fi amr al-nasab).
Istihsan overrides the qiyas for a higher purpose.
4
Analyze the Scope of the Exception
If the woman had claimed marriage without a child, the son's evidence would prevail. The presence of a child (lineage) triggers the istihsan. Also, Abu Hanifa does not nullify the son's evidence—both testimonies stand, but lineage is established.
The exception is narrow: only when lineage is at stake.
5
Resolve the Textual Variation
Al-Ramli notes that in some transmissions, Abu Hanifa nullifies the son's evidence. This variation affects the practical outcome. The relied-upon view seems to be that the son's evidence is not nullified.
The negation particle 'la' may be extra (ziyada) in some versions.

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explaining the distinction between the day of death and the day of killing regarding judicial acceptance of testimony. The rule is that the day of death does not 'enter under judicial consideration,' meaning that if testimony about the day of death contradicts other established facts (e.g., a marriage after that day), it is not accepted. Conversely, the day of killing does enter, so testimony about the day of killing is accepted as long as it does not conflict with subsequent events. The commentator presents branches from al-Bazzaziyyah: if an heir proves death on a day, and a woman proves marriage after that day, the marriage is upheld; if an heir proves killing on a day, and a woman proves marriage after that day, the marriage is not accepted because killing is taken as definitive. Al-Walwalji clarifies with an analogy: if a woman proves the man was in Mecca on the day of sacrifice, and another proves marriage on the same day in Khurasan, the second is rejected because the first is conclusive. Al-Ramli explains the similarity. The passage then presents a case from al-Zahiriyyah involving conflicting death dates in an inheritance dispute; some scholars accept the defense based on the rule, others reject it. A second case from al-Zahiriyyah involves an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa uses istihsan to accept a woman's evidence establishing lineage over a son's evidence of a killing, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad follow qiyas (analogy) and would give precedence to the son's evidence. The text notes that caution in lineage justifies the istihsan, and Abu Hanifa does not nullify the son's evidence. Al-Ramli clarifies that in some reports, Abu Hanifa does nullify the son's evidence, meaning the negation in the text may be a scribal error. The overall lesson shows exceptions to the general rule.

Key Terms
يوم الموت (yawm al-mawt): The day of death; not definitive in judicial testimony.
يوم القتل (yawm al-qatl): The day of killing; definitive in judicial testimony.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference overriding qiyas for equity or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the istihsan case, what additional condition triggers Abu Hanifa's exception?
A) The woman must be wealthy.
B) The woman must bring a child.
C) The killing must be intentional.
D) The marriage must be proven by four witnesses.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa uses istihsan to protect lineage, overriding the definitive day of killing rule when a child is involved, while the Sahibayn adhere to qiyas.

Defeating a Purchase Claim by Proving Earlier Death
Procedural ruling on daf' al-da'wa with time-of-death evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the admissibility of evidence proving a prior death in a claim of purchase from a deceased father and apply it to similar procedural scenarios.

Core Idea
Evidence of earlier death defeats a later purchase claim because the time of death is not judicially countable.

In Hanafi judicial procedure, timing can be decisive. This lesson presents a specific ruling from al-Qunyah: if a defendant proves the seller died before the claimed purchase date, the claim is rejected. The underlying maxim is that the time of death does not fall under judicial consideration, an exception to general principles. Understanding this rule helps prevent fraudulent claims against heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Recognize the plaintiff's claim: he purchased an item from a deceased father a certain number of years ago. The father is currently dead. The defendant (possessor) counters with evidence that the father died earlier than the claimed purchase date.
2
Recognize the Procedural Mechanism
This is daf' al-da'wa (repelling the claim). The defendant uses evidence to show the claim is factually impossible, thus the claim is rejected.
In Hanafi law, the possessor (dhu al-yad) is given priority in evidence, but here the evidence establishes a clear timeline contradiction.
3
Understand the Key Maxim
The text states 'the time of death does not enter under judicial consideration' (zaman al-mawt la yadkhul tahta al-qada). This means that when evaluating facts, the exact moment of death is not precisely counted in court; however, when a proven earlier death makes a later transaction impossible, the defense is accepted as an exception.
This is parallel to the maxim about 'the day of death' not entering, but extends to the entire time period.
4
Note the Exception
Some scholars consider this a second exception: the rule that 'the day of death does not enter' is extended to 'the time of death does not enter', allowing the defense based on proving earlier death.
This exception ensures justice by preventing impossible claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية من باب دفع الدعوى : ادعى عليه شيئاً أنه اشتراه من أبيه منذ عشر سنين والأب ميت للحال فأقام ذو اليد البينة أنه مات منذ عشرين سنة تسمع . قال أستاذنا رضي الله عنه : والصواب جواب الحافظ فينبغي أن يحفظ فإنه كان يحفظ أن زمان الموت لا يدخل تحت القضاء ا هـ . وهي ثانية تستثنى على قول البعض من قولهم يوم الموت لا يدخل أن زمان الموت لا يدخل.
And in al-Qunyah from the chapter of repelling the claim: One claimed against him something that he had purchased from his father twenty years ago, and the father is deceased at present. The possessor presented evidence that he died twenty years ago. It is heard. Our teacher, may Allah be pleased with him, said: And the correct answer is that of al-Hafiz, so it should be memorized, for he used to say that the time of death does not enter under judicial consideration. End quote. And it is a second exception according to some from their statement that the day of death does not enter, that the time of death does not enter.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage from al-Qunyah presents a ruling in the chapter of repelling a claim (daf' al-da'wa). If someone claims to have purchased an item from a deceased father twenty years ago while the father is currently dead, and the possessor of the item (the defendant) presents evidence that the father died twenty years ago (i.e., before the claimed purchase), the claim is heard and accepted. The commentator's teacher says this follows the opinion of al-Hafiz, who held that the time of death does not enter under judicial consideration—parallel to the earlier rule about the day of death. This is an exception to the general principle for some scholars, as it allows the defense based on proving earlier death.

Key Terms
دفع الدعوى (daf' al-da'wa): A defense mechanism where the defendant presents evidence to refute the plaintiff's claim, often by proving a contradictory fact.
ذو اليد (dhu al-yad): The person who has possession of the item; here, the defendant who possesses the purchased item.
تسمع (tasmau): It is heard; meaning the evidence is accepted and considered by the court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Qunyah, why is the defendant's evidence of the father's earlier death heard?
A) Because the possessor always has the stronger evidence.
B) Because the time of death does not enter under judicial consideration, allowing the defense.
C) Because the claim is about a deceased person.
D) Because the plaintiff's claim is not credible.

Key Takeaway
When the defendant proves the deceased seller died before the claimed purchase date, the claim is rejected because the time of death is not judicially countable, an exception that prevents impossible claims.

Conflicting Testimony on Killings: Independent Claims and Preferring Latest Evidence
Discusses cases of conflicting testimony on killings and the principle of preferring the latest evidence if it is well-known.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for conflicting testimony on killings and explain the principle of preferring the most recent well-known evidence.

Core Idea
Independent claims on different killers are accepted; latest widely-known fact overrides earlier individual testimony.

Testimony about killings can conflict in several ways. This passage from Khizanat al-Akmal presents two key rulings: one for multiple independent killers on the same day, and another for a single killer accused of two simultaneous murders. It also introduces a crucial Hanafi evidentiary principle: when chronological evidence conflicts, prefer the more recent fact if it is well-known. These rules illustrate how the Hanafi school balances individual testimony with public knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two conflict scenarios
The passage first addresses a case where two different killers are accused of killing two different victims on the same day but in different cities. Then it considers a case where one killer is accused of killing two different victims at the same time.
The key variable is whether the killer is the same person or different persons.
2
Understand the ruling for multiple independent killers
If each claimant proves a different killer killed his father on the same day in different cities, both claims are accepted. Each killer pays half the diyah (blood money). The day of killing is judicially acknowledged.
This ruling is from Nawadir Ibn Rustam, a non-zahir al-riwayah source.
3
Understand the ruling for a single killer with multiple victims
If the same person is accused of killing two different victims on the same day but in different locations (e.g., Mecca and Kufa), neither claim is accepted because it is impossible for one person to be in two places at the same time.
This is the principle of physical impossibility.
4
Apply the principle of preferring latest evidence
When a plaintiff claims a killing occurred a year ago, and the defendant proves the victim led Friday prayers last week (showing he was alive after), Abu Hanifa says the more recent evidence takes precedence, provided it is well-known (mashhur).
The condition 'mashhur' is essential: the later fact must be widely known to override individual testimony.
5
Recognize the Ramli qualification
Al-Ramli qualifies that this principle applies generally: if a fact (like a death) is widely known, it outweighs individual testimony. He cites a case where a judge's widely-known death before a trial date defeats a witness claim.
This shows the strength of common knowledge in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي خزانة الأكمل بعد ما ذكر أن يوم الموت لا يدخل ويوم القتل يدخل قال : ولو أقام رجل البينة أن هذا قتل أبي يوم النحر بمكة وأقام أخو هذا المدعي بينة على رجل آخر أنه قتل أبي يوسف النحر بالكوفة جازت ويحكم لكل واحد منهما بنصف الدية، أما لو كان القاتل واحداً والمقتول اثنين لم تقبل؛ ذكره في نوادر ابن رستم عن محمد ا . ثم قال : ولو أقام رجل البينة أنه قتل أبي منذ سنة وأقام المشهود عليه بينة أن أباه صلي بالناس الجمعة الماضية قال أبو حنيفة : الأخذ بالأحدث أولى إن كان شيئاً مشهوراً ! قوله : (أما لو كان القاتل واحداً والمقتول اثنين لم تقبل) قال الرملي : يعني لو ادعى أن هذا قتل أبي زيداً . النحر بمكة يوم وادعى آخر أنه قتل عمراً يوم النحر بالكوفة لا يجوز ولا يحكم لواحد منهما. قوله : (الأخذ بالأحدث أولى إن كان شيئاً مشهوراً) قال الرملي وهذا يقيد به ما مضى أيضاً وهذا قيد لازم لا بد منه حتى لو اشتهر موت رجل عند الناس فادعى رجل أنه اشترى منه داره منذ سنة وكان موته قد اشتهر عند الناس منذ عشرين سنة فدفعه بذلك يجب قبوله لما ذكر تأمل. ثم بفضل الله تعالى ومنته رأيت ما يشهد به صريحاً قال في التتارخانية في الفصل الثامن في التهاتر نقلاً عن الذخيرة فيما لو ادعى المشهود عليه أن الشهود محدودون في قذف من قاضي بلد كذا فأقام الشهود أنه أي القاضي سنة كذا الخ أنه لا يقضى به إذا كان موت القاضي قبل تاريخ شهود المدعى عليه مستفيضاً اهـ. مع
And in Khizanat al-Akmal, after mentioning that the day of death does not enter and the day of killing enters, he said: If a man presents evidence that this man killed my father on the day of sacrifice in Mecca, and the brother of this claimant presents evidence against another man that he killed my father Yusuf on the day of sacrifice in Kufa, it is permitted and each is judged to pay half the blood money. But if the killer is one and the victim is two, it is not accepted; this was mentioned in Nawadir Ibn Rustam from Muhammad. Then he said: If a man presents evidence that he killed my father a year ago, and the defendant presents evidence that his father led the people in prayer last Friday, Abu Hanifa said: The taking of the more recent is better if it is a well-known matter. His saying: (But if the killer is one and the victim is two, it is not accepted) al-Ramli said: meaning if one claims that this man killed my father Zayd on the day of sacrifice in Mecca, and another claims that he killed Amr on the day of sacrifice in Kufa, it is not permissible and no judgment is given for either. His saying: (The taking of the more recent is better if it is a well-known matter) al-Ramli said: And this qualifies what has passed before, and this is a necessary qualification, such that if the death of a man is widely known among people, and a man claims that he bought his house from him a year ago, while his death was widely known among people twenty years ago, and he repels it with that, it must be accepted for what was mentioned; ponder. Then, by Allah's grace and favor, I saw what testifies clearly to it: he said in al-Tatar-Khaniyyah in the eighth chapter on al-tahatur, quoting from al-Dhakhirah, regarding the case where the defendant claims that the witnesses are hadd-punished for slander by a judge of such-and-such a country, and the witnesses prove that the judge died in such-and-such a year, etc., that it is not judged if the death of the judge before the date of the plaintiff's witnesses is widespread. End quote.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage from Khizanat al-Akmal presents two rulings on testimony regarding killing. First: if two different men claim that two different people killed their respective fathers on the same day (the day of sacrifice) but in different locations (Mecca and Kufa), both claims are accepted, and each killer pays half the diyah (blood money). This is because each claim is independent and the day of killing enters judicial consideration. However, if the killer is one person but the victims are two different people (i.e., one claim that the killer killed Zayd, and another that the same killer killed Amr), then neither claim is accepted due to the impossibility of being in two places at once. This is from Nawadir Ibn Rustam from Muhammad. Second: if a plaintiff claims his father was killed a year ago, and the defendant proves his father led Friday prayers last week (showing he was alive after the claimed killing), Abu Hanifa says the more recent evidence (the Friday prayer testimony) is to be preferred, provided it is well-known (mashhur). Al-Ramli qualifies this, stating that this condition applies to all similar cases: if a fact is widely known (like a death), it takes precedence over individual testimony. He cites an example from al-Tatar-Khaniyyah about a judge's death being widely known, which overrides contradictory testimony.

Key Terms
نوادر ابن رستم (nawadir Ibn Rustam): Rare transmissions from Imam Muhammad through Ibn Rustam, considered part of the nawadir (non-zahir al-riwayah) sources in the Hanafi school.
الأخذ بالأحدث (al-akhdh bi al-ahdath): The principle of preferring the most recent evidence when there is a chronological conflict, provided the later fact is well-known.
مشهوراً (mashhuran): A matter that is widely known and publicly recognized, so it carries greater evidentiary weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if two different men claim that two different persons killed their fathers on the same day in different cities?
A) Both claims are rejected because the day of killing cannot be established.
B) Only the first claim is accepted.
C) Both claims are accepted, and each killer pays half the blood money.
D) The matter is referred to the ruler for investigation.

Key Takeaway
Conflicting testimony on killings is resolved by logical possibility: independent claims are accepted, but the latest well-known fact overrides earlier individual evidence.

Classification of Division Methods in Hanafi Law: Cases and Principles
Expanding a principle of division with numerous examples and intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a given claim scenario into one of the four division methods by applying the Hanafi principle of simultaneous vs. successive establishment of rights.

Core Idea
Division method depends on whether rights arise together (ʿawl) or separately (munāzaʿa).

This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq presents a comprehensive taxonomy of division methods (qisma) in Hanafi law. When multiple parties claim shares in a single asset, the law distinguishes between proportional reduction (ʿawl) and contestation (munāzaʿa) based on whether the rights are established simultaneously or at different times. The text enumerates numerous concrete examples from inheritance, debts, bequests, and torts, and highlights an intra-school difference between Imam Abū Ḥanīfa and his two disciples (Ṣāḥibayn). Understanding this classification equips you to resolve complex property disputes with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
Read Qāḍīkhān's statement that division issues are of four types: (1) unanimously by ʿawl, (2) unanimously by munāzaʿa, (3) munāzaʿa according to Abū Ḥanīfa and ʿawl according to the Ṣāḥibayn, (4) the reverse. Note the eight cases in the first category, one case in the second, three in the third, and five in the fourth.
The first category includes inheritance, debts, various bequests, and torts by slaves.
2
Analyze the unanimously agreed cases
For the first eight cases, all imams agree on ʿawl. For the single second case (fudūlī sale), all agree on munāzaʿa. Understand why: in the first group, rights are established simultaneously (e.g., at death, at surrender); in the second, rights arise from separate contracts at different times.
The fudūlī case: two meddlers sell the same slave; ownership vests upon ratification, which occurs at different times.
3
Examine the disputed categories
The third category (Abū Ḥanīfa: munāzaʿa, Ṣāḥibayn: ʿawl) includes the house dispute and similar bequest cases. The fourth category (Abū Ḥanīfa: ʿawl, Ṣāḥibayn: munāzaʿa) includes cases of the licensed slave (maʾdhūn), torts by slaves, and the umm walad. For each, note the actual share outcomes (e.g., 3/4 vs. 2/3).
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilāf) affects the distributive shares.
4
Understand the Ṣāḥibayn's principle
The text gives the asl: if two rights are established on a shared basis (shuyūʿ) at one time, division is by ʿawl; if established distinctly or at different times, division is by munāzaʿa. This is supported by the ijmaʿ of the Companions on ʿawl in inheritance, extended by analogy to similar cases.
The prohibition of taking both whole and half from one property is the qiyās argument, overridden by ijmaʿ.
5
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical case (e.g., two torts from one slave at the same moment), classify the division method using the Ṣāḥibayn's principle. Confirm with the examples already studied.
This step reinforces the operational use of the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

فاعتبر طريق العول والمضاربة فصاحب الجميع يضرب بكل حقه سهمين وصاحب النصف بسهم واحد فيقسم أثلاثاً. وذكر في الهداية أن لهذه المسألة نظائر وأضداداً لا يحتملها هذا المختصر وقد ذكرناها في الزيادات اهـ. وذكر المؤلف في الكافي بعضها وقال: وسيجيء في كتاب الديات على الاستقصاء مع الأصول إن شاء الله تعالى .اهـ. واختصر الشارح مسائلها وقال : وبيان طرق هذه المسائل وتخريجها على هذه الأصول وتمام تفريعها مذكور في شرح الزيادات لقاضيخان .اهـ. وقد يسر الله تعالى لي بشرح الزيادات لقاضيخان قبيل تأليف هذا المحل فأحببت أن أنقلها منه بألفاظه فأقول مستعيناً بالله قال قاضيخان في هذا الشرح من كتاب الجنايات من باب جناية أم الولد على مولاها وعلى غيره وجنس مسائل القسمة أربع، منها ما يقسم بطريق العول والمضاربة عند الكل، ومنها ما يقسم بطريق المنازعة عندهم، ومنها ما يقسم بطريق المنازعة عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما بطريق العول والمضاربة، ومنها ما يقسم على عكس ذلك. أما ما يقسم بطريق العول عندهم ثمانٍ : إحداها الميراث إذا اجتمعت سهام الفرائض في التركة وضاقت التركة عن الوفاء بها تقسم التركة بين أرباب الديون على طريق العول. والثانية إذا اجتمعت الديون المتفاوتة وضاقت التركة عن الوفاء بها تقسم التركة بين أرباب الديون بطريق العول. والثالثة إذا أوصى لرجل بثلث ماله ولآخر ماله ولآخر بربع بسدس ماله ولم تجز الورثة حتى عادت الوصايا إلى الثلث يقسم الثلث بينهم على طريق العول. والرابعة الوصية بالمحاباة إذا أوصى أن يباع العبد الذي قيمته ثلاثة آلاف درهم من هذا الرجل بألفي درهم وأوصى لآخر أن يباع منه العبد الذي يساوي ألفي درهم بألف درهم حتى حصلت المحاباة لهما بألفي درهم كان الثلث بينهما بطريق العول. والخامسة الوصية بالعتق إذا أوصى بأن يعتق من هذا العبد نصفه وأوصى بأن يعتق من هذا الآخر ثلثه وذاك لا يخرج من الثلث يقسم ثلث المال بينهما بطريق العول ويسقط من كل واحد منهما حصته من السعاية والسادسة الوصية بألف مرسلة إذا أوصى لرجل بألف ولآخر بألفين كان الثلث بينهما بطريق العول والسابعة عبد فقأ عين رجل وقتل آخر خطأ فدفع بهما يقسم الجاني بينهما بطريق العول ثلثاه لولي القتيل وثلثه للآخر . والثامنة مدبر جنى على هذا الوجه ودفعت القيمة إلى أولياء الجناية كانت القيمة بينهما بطريق العول. وأما ما يقسم بطريق المنازعة عندهم مسألة واحدة ذكرها في جامع الفصولين : فضولي باع عبداً من رجل بألف درهم وفضولي آخر باع نصفه من آخر بخمسمائة فأجاز المولى البيعين جميعاً يخير المشتريان، فإن اختارا الأخذ أخذاً بطريق المنازعة ثلاثة أرباعه لمشتري الكل وربعه لمشتري النصف جميعاً . عندهم وأما ما يقسم بطريق المنازعة عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما بطريق العول ثلاث مسائل : إحداها دار تنازع فيها رجلان أحدهما يدعي كلها والآخر يدعي نصفها وأقاما البينة عند أبي حنيفة تقسم الدار بينهما بطريق المنازعة ثلاثة أرباعها لمدعي الكل والربع لمدعي النصف، وعندهما أثلاثاً ثلثاها لمدعي الكل وثلثها لمدعي النصف . والثانية إذا أوصى بجميع ماله لرجل ونصفه لآخر وأجازت الورثة عند أبي حنيفة المال بينهما أرباعاً وعندهما أثلاثاً. والثالثة إذا أوصى بعبد بعينه لرجل وبنصفه الآخر وهو يخرج من ثلثه أولا يخرج وأجازت الورثة كان العبد بينهما أرباعاً عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما أثلاثاً وأما ما يقسم بطريق العول عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما بطريق المنازعة خمس مسائل ؛ منها ما ذكره في المأذون : عبد مأذون بين رجلين أدانه أحد الموليين مائة يعني باعه شيئاً بنسيئة وأدانه أجنبي مائة فبيع العبد بمائة عند أبي حنيفة يقسم ثمن العبد بين المولى المدين وبين الأجنبي أثلاثاً ثلثاه للأجنبي وثلثه للمولى لأن إدانته تصح في نصيب شريكه لا في نصيبه والثانية إذا أدانه أجنبي مائة وأجنبي آخر خمسين وبيع العبد عند أبي حنيفة يقسم الثمن بينهما أثلاثاً وعندهما أرباعاً والثالثة عبد قتل رجلاً خطأ وآخر عمداً وللمقتول عمداً وليان فعفا أحدهما يخير مولى العبد بين الدفع والفداء فإن هذا المولى يفدى بخمسة عشر ألفاً خمسة آلاف لشريكه العافي وعشرة آلاف لولي الخطأ، فإن دفع يقسم العبد بينهما أثلاثاً عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما أرباعاً. والرابعة لو كان الجاني مدبراً والمسألة بحالها ودفع المولى القيمة. والخامسة مسألة الكتاب أم ولد قتلت مولاها وأجنبياً عمداً ولكل واحد منهما وليان فعفا أحد وليي كل واحد منهما على التعاقب سعت في ثلاثة أرباع قيمتها كان للساكت من وليي الأجنبي ربع القيمة ويقسم نصف القيمة بينهما بطريق العول أثلاثاً عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما أرباعاً بطريق المنازعة والأصل لأبي يوسف ومحمد أن الحقين متى ثبتا على الشيوع في وقت واحد كانت القسمة عولية، وإن ثبتا على وجه التمييز أو في وقتين مختلفين كانت القسمة نزاعية والمعنى فيه أن القياس يأبى القسمة بطريق العول لأن تفسير العول أن يضرب كل واحد منهما بجميع حقه أحدهما بنصف المال والآخر بالكل والمال الواحد لا يكون له كل ونصف آخر ولهذا قال ابن عباس : من شاء باهلته إن الله لم يجعل في المال الواحد ثلثين ونصفاً ولا نصفين وثلثاً. وإنما تركنا القياس في الميراث بإجماع الصحابة فيلحق به ما كان في معناه وفي الميراث حقوق الكل بنيت على وجه الشيوع في وقت واحد وهو حالة الموت وفي التركة إذا اجتمعت حقوق متفاوتة حق أرباب الديون ويثبت في وقت واحد وهو حالة الموت أو المرض فكانت في معنى الميراث، وكذلك في الوصايا. وفي العبد والمدبر إذا فقأ عين إنسان وقتل آخر خطأ حق أصحاب الجناية ثبت في وقت وهو وقت دفع العبد الجناية أو قيمة المدبر لأن موجب جناية الخطأ لا يملك قبل الدفع. ولهذا لا يجب فيه الزكاة قبل القبض ولا تصح به الكفالة وإنما يملك عند التسليم ووقت الدفع واحد. وفي مسألة دعوى الدار الحق إنما ثبت بالقضاء ووقت القضاء واحد فكانت في معنى مسألة الميراث، وفي بيع الفضولي وقت ثبوت الحقين مختلف لأن الملك ثبت عند الإجازة
Book of Claims, Chapter on Claim of Two Men. So consider the method of 'awl and mudaraba: the owner of all strikes with his full right two shares, and the owner of half one share, so it is divided into three. It was mentioned in al-Hidayah that this issue has parallels and opposites that this abridgement cannot contain, and we have mentioned them in al-Ziyadat. The author mentioned some of them in al-Kafi and said: It will come in the Book of Blood-Money (Diyat) thoroughly with the principles, God willing. The commentator abbreviated its issues and said: The explanation of the methods of these issues, their derivation from these principles, and the complete elaboration of their branches are mentioned in the Commentary on al-Ziyadat by Qadikhan. God facilitated for me the Commentary on al-Ziyadat by Qadikhan shortly before composing this place, so I wished to quote them from it in his words, so I say, seeking help from God: Qadikhan said in this commentary, from the Book of Torts (Jinayat), from the Chapter on the Tort of a Umm al-Walad (mother of a child) against her master and against others: The genus of division issues is four: among them what is divided by the method of 'awl and mudaraba according to all; among them what is divided by the method of munaza'a (contestation) according to them; among them what is divided by the method of munaza'a according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) by the method of 'awl and mudaraba; and among them what is divided conversely to that. As for what is divided by 'awl according to them: eight issues. First: Inheritance—if the shares of fixed portions meet in the estate and the estate is insufficient to fulfill them, the estate is divided among the owners of debts (heirs with fixed shares) by the method of 'awl. Second: If varying debts meet and the estate is insufficient to fulfill them, the estate is divided among the creditors by the method of 'awl. Third: If a person bequeaths to a man one-third of his wealth, to another his entire wealth, and to another a quarter or a sixth of his wealth, and the heirs do not consent, so the bequests revert to one-third, then the one-third is divided among them by 'awl. Fourth: Bequest of partiality (muhabah): If he bequeaths that a slave worth 3000 dirhams be sold to this man for 2000 dirhams, and bequeaths to another that the slave worth 2000 dirhams be sold to him for 1000 dirhams, so that the partiality for both amounts to 2000 dirhams, then the one-third is divided between them by 'awl. Fifth: Bequest of manumission: If he bequeaths that half of this slave be freed, and bequeaths that one-third of that other be freed, and that is not covered by one-third, then one-third of the wealth is divided between them by 'awl, and from each of them his share of the earnings (sa'aya) is dropped. Sixth: Bequest of a specific one thousand: If he bequeaths to a man one thousand and to another two thousand, the one-third is divided between them by 'awl. Seventh: A slave gouged out a man's eye and killed another by mistake, and the slave is surrendered for both: the perpetrator is divided between them by 'awl: two-thirds for the guardian of the slain and one-third for the other. Eighth: A mudabbar (slave with posthumous freedom) incurred an injury in this manner, and the value is paid to the guardians of the injury: the value is divided between them by 'awl. As for what is divided by munaza'a according to them: one issue, mentioned in Jami' al-Fusulayn: A meddler (fuduli) sold a slave to a man for one thousand dirhams, and another meddler sold half of him to another for five hundred dirhams, and the master ratified both sales: the two buyers are given the choice; if they choose to take, they take by munaza'a: three-quarters for the buyer of the whole and one-quarter for the buyer of the half together. According to them. And what is divided by munaza'a according to Abu Hanifa, and by 'awl according to them: three issues. First: A house in which two men are in dispute: one claims all of it, the other claims half of it, and they present evidence: according to Abu Hanifa, the house is divided between them by munaza'a: three-quarters for the claimant of all, and one-quarter for the claimant of half; according to them, into three: two-thirds for the claimant of all, one-third for the claimant of half. Second: If he bequeaths all his wealth to a man and half of it to another, and the heirs consent: according to Abu Hanifa, the wealth is divided between them into fourths; according to them, into thirds. Third: If he bequeaths a specific slave to a man and the other half of him to another, whether it comes out of one-third or not, and the heirs consent: the slave is divided between them into fourths according to Abu Hanifa, and into thirds according to them. And what is divided by 'awl according to Abu Hanifa, and by munaza'a according to them: five issues: among them what is mentioned in al-Ma'dhun: a slave licensed to trade (ma'dhun) owned jointly by two men: one of the two owners lent him one hundred—meaning he sold him something on credit—and a stranger lent him one hundred; then the slave was sold for one hundred: according to Abu Hanifa, the price of the slave is divided between the creditor owner and the stranger into three: two-thirds for the stranger, one-third for the owner, because his loan is valid in his partner's share, not in his own share. Second: If a stranger lent him one hundred and another stranger lent him fifty, and the slave is sold: according to Abu Hanifa, the price is divided between them into three; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), into four. Third: A slave killed a man by mistake and another intentionally, and the victim of intentional killing has two guardians, and one of them pardons: the slave's owner is given the choice between surrendering the slave and paying ransom; then if he pays ransom, he ransoms him for fifteen thousand: five thousand for his pardoning partner, and ten thousand for the guardian of the mistaken killing; if he surrenders the slave, the slave is divided between them into three according to Abu Hanifa, and into four according to them. Fourth: If the perpetrator was a mudabbar, and the issue is as before, and the owner pays the value. Fifth: The issue of the text (Book): a slave girl (umm walad) killed her master and a stranger intentionally, and each of them has two guardians, and one of the two guardians of each of them pardons successively: she works (sa't) for three-fourths of her value; the silent one among the guardians of the stranger gets a quarter of the value, and half of the value is divided between them by 'awl into three according to Abu Hanifa, and into four according to them by munaza'a. The principle (asl) according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is: whenever two rights are established on a shared basis (shuyu') at one time, the division is by 'awl; if they are established distinctly or at two different times, the division is by munaza'a. The meaning is that analogy (qiyas) rejects division by 'awl because the interpretation of 'awl is that each of the two strikes with his full right: one with half the property and the other with the whole, and a single property cannot be both whole and half. That is why Ibn Abbas said: "Whoever wishes, I will invoke a curse (mubahala) upon him: verily God has not made in a single property two-thirds and a half, nor two-halves and a third." We only abandoned qiyas in inheritance due to the consensus (ijma) of the Companions, so what is in its meaning is annexed to it. In inheritance, the rights of all are built on a shared basis at one time, which is the state of death. In the estate, if varying rights of creditors meet, they are established at one time (state of death or illness), so it is in the meaning of inheritance—similarly for bequests. In the case of the slave and mudabbar who gouged out a man's eye and killed another by mistake, the right of the owners of the injury is established at one time: the time of surrendering the slave for the injury or the value of the mudabbar, because the obligation of accidental killing is not owned before surrender. Therefore, zakah is not due on it before possession, nor is guaranty (kafala) valid with it; it is only owned upon delivery, and the time of delivery is one. In the issue of the claim of the house, the right is established only by judgment, and the time of judgment is one, so it is in the meaning of the inheritance issue. In the sale by a meddler (fuduli), the time of establishment of the two rights is different, because ownership is established upon ratification.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion on the methods of division (qisma) in various legal contexts. The author first establishes the immediate ruling: when a person claims all and another claims half of a property, according to the principle of 'awl and mudaraba, the division is in three shares: the claimant of all gets two, the claimant of half gets one. He then references al-Hidayah and other works, noting that detailed treatment of all related cases can be found in Qadikhan's Commentary on al-Ziyadat. The author quotes Qadikhan extensively. Qadikhan classifies division cases into four categories: (1) those divided by 'awl and mudaraba according to all; (2) those divided by munaza'a (contestation) according to all; (3) those divided by munaza'a according to Abu Hanifa but by 'awl according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); and (4) the reverse: 'awl according to Abu Hanifa but munaza'a according to the Sahibayn. Eight specific cases are listed for the first category, including inheritance with multiple fixed shares, multiple debts, various bequests, and torts by slaves. One case (fuduli sale) is given for the second category. Three cases (disputes over a house, bequests of all and half, and bequest of a specific slave) illustrate the third category where Abu Hanifa favors munaza'a and the Sahibayn favor 'awl. Five cases (from the chapter on the licensed slave, torts of slaves, and the umm walad) illustrate the fourth category where Abu Hanifa favors 'awl and the Sahibayn favor munaza'a. The underlying principle is then explained: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, if two rights are established concurrently and coextensively (on shuyu'), division is by 'awl; if they are established distinctly or at different times, division is by munaza'a. Analogy ('awl) is against division by 'awl because one property cannot be simultaneously whole and half. However, consensus (ijma) of the Companions established 'awl in inheritance, and it is extended to similar cases where rights arise at a single moment. Examples include the rights of heirs at death, creditors at death or illness, recipients of bequests at death, and victims of tort at the time of surrender of the slave. In the house dispute, rights are established by the single judgment, so it is like inheritance. In fuduli sale, rights are established at different times (ratification), so munaza'a applies.

Key Terms
العول (al-ʿawl): A method of proportional reduction used when total shares exceed the estate; each heir's share is reduced proportionally.
المضاربة (al-muḍāraba): In this context, a method of division where each party's share is determined by multiplying their claim by the total property and dividing by total claims, synonymous with ʿawl.
المنازعة (al-munāzaʿa): A method of division by contestation, where the property is divided as per the disputed portions, resulting in unequal shares without proportional reduction.
الشيوع (al-shuyūʿ): Shared or undivided ownership; here it refers to rights being held coextensively in the same thing at the same time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle of Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad, what determines whether division is by ʿawl or munāzaʿa?
A) The amount of the claim
B) The number of parties involved
C) Whether the rights are established simultaneously or at different times
D) The consent of the parties

Key Takeaway
The Hanafī school classifies division methods into ʿawl (proportional reduction) and munāzaʿa (contestation) based on whether the competing rights are established simultaneously or at different times, with the Ṣāḥibayn's principle serving as the primary framework for extension.

advanced
12 min
The 'Awl and Munaza'a Division Principles: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on division methods for competing claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'awl and munaza'a division methods and apply Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's criteria to determine which method governs a given set of competing claims.

Core Idea
'Awl applies when rights are in the dhimma or a common part; Munaza'a when rights are distinct or established at different times.

When multiple claimants have rights in a single property, how do we divide it? The Hanafi school has two methods: 'awl (proportional reduction) and munaza'a (distribution by litigation). This lesson explores the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, over which method applies in various scenarios. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to reason about competing claims by analyzing the nature and timing of the underlying rights.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two division methods
Learn what 'awl and munaza'a mean. 'Awl reduces each claim proportionally when they exceed the property. Munaza'a gives each claimant a distinct portion based on the strength of their specific claim, without proportional reduction.
2
Identify the core principle of each imam
Abu Hanifa focuses on the nature of the right: if the right is established in the dhimma (liability) or in a common part of the property, 'awl applies. The Sahibayn focus on timing and commonality: 'awl applies only if both rights are established simultaneously on a common basis; otherwise munaza'a.
3
Map the five scenarios from the text
Review the five cases: bequests, credits of a jointly-owned slave, injuries by a slave, mudabbir, and umm walad. For each, note the method according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
The practical difference appears in the shares: e.g., bequest to A (all) and B (half) yields fourths vs thirds.
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each position
Abu Hanifa argues by analogy to inheritance, where 'awl is permitted by ijma. He extends the 'illa of 'common right' to rights in the dhimma. The Sahibayn counter that inheritance is unique; 'awl requires true simultaneity and commonality, which is absent when rights arise at different times.
The Sahibayn rely on the impossibility of a single property being wholly owned by two, as Ibn Abbas stated.
5
Apply the principles to a new case
Given a new scenario (e.g., two creditors with debts from different dates against a single debtor's asset), determine whether 'awl or munaza'a would apply under each imam's view. State the resulting shares.

كتاب الدعوى باب دعوى الرجلين أوصى . وعندهما أثلاثاً ثلثاها لمدعي الكل وثلثها لمدعي النصف . والثانية إذا أوصى بجميع ماله لرجل ونصفه لآخر وأجازت الورثة عند أبي حنيفة المال بينهما أرباعاً وعندهما الجناية أو قيمة المدبر لأن موجب جناية الخطأ لا يملك قبل الدفع. ولهذا لا يجب فيه الزكاة قبل القبض ولا تصح به الكفالة وإنما يملك عند التسليم ووقت الدفع واحد. وفي مسألة دعوى الدار الحق إنما ثبت بالقضاء ووقت القضاء واحد فكانت في معنى مسألة الميراث، وفي بيع الفضولي وقت ثبوت الحقين مختلف لأن الملك ثبت عند الإجازة مستنداً إلى وقت العقد ووقت العقد مختلف. وفي القسم الرابع وقت ثبوت الحقين مختلف، في مسألة الإدانة فلأن الحق ثبت بالإدانة ووقت الإدانة مختلف. وفي العبد إذا قتل رجلاً عمداً وآخر خطأ وللمقتول عمداً وليان فعفا أحدهما واختار المولى دفع العبد أو كان الجاني مدبراً والمسألة بحالها فدفع المولى القيمة عندهما يقسم بطريق المنازعة لأن وقت ثبوت الحقين مختلف لأن حق الساكت من وليي الدم كان في القصاص لأنه مثل، والمال بدل عن القصاص ووجوب البدل مضاف إلى سبب الأصل وهو القتل فكان وقت ثبوت حقه القتل وحق ولي الخطأ في القيمة إذ العبد المدفوع يثبت عند الدفع لا قبله لأنه صلة معنى والصلات لا تملك قبل القبض فكان وقت الحقين مختلفاً فلم يكن في معنى الميراث وكانت القسمة نزاعية. وفي جناية أم الولد وجوب الدية للذي لم يعف مضاف إلى القتل لما قلنا، والقتلان وجدا في وقتين مختلفين فكانت القسمة نزاعية عندهما والأصل لأبي حنيفة أن قسمة العين متى كانت بحق ثابت في الذمة أو بحق ثبت في العين على وجه الشيوع في البعض دون الكل كانت القسمة عولية، ومتى وجبت قسمة العين بحق ثبت على وجه التمييز أو كان حق أحدهما في البعض الشائع وحق الآخر في الكل كانت القسمة نزاعية والمعنى فيه أن الحقوق متى وجبت في الذمة فقد استوت في القوّة لأن الذمة متسعة فيضرب كل واحد منهما بجميع في العين . كذا إذا كان حق كل واحد في العين لكن في الجزء الشائع فقد استوت في القوة لأن ما من جزء ثبت فيه حق أحدهما إلا وللآخر أن يزاحمه فكانت الحقوق مستوية في القوة والأصل في العول الميراث كما قالا وثمة حق كل واحد منهم ثبت في البعض الشائع، وإذا ثبت الحقان على وجه التمييز لم يكن في معنى الميراث. وكذا إذا كان حق أحدهما في البعض الشائع وحق الآخر في الكل لم يكن في معنى الميراث لأن صاحب الكل يزاحم صاحب البعض في كل شيء، أما صاحب البعض لا يزاحم صاحبه في الكل فلم يكن في معنى الميراث، ولأن حق كل واحد منهما إذا كان في البعض الشائع وما يأخذ كل واحد منهما بحكم القسمة غير مفرز وأنه غير الشائع كان المأخوذ بدل حقه لا أصل حقه فيكون في معنى الميراث والتركة التي اجتمعت فيها الديون. وفي مسائل القسمة إنما وجبت بحق ثابت في الذمة لأن حق كل واحد منهما في موجب الجناية وموجب الجناية يكون في الذمة فكانت القسمة فيها عولية، فعلى هذا تخرج المسائل. هذا إذا لم يكن لها ولد من المولى، فإن كان لها ولد من المولى يرثه فلا قصاص عليها بدم المولى لأن الولد لا يستوجب القصاص على والديه ولهذا لو قتلت المرأة ولدها لا يجب عليها القصاص لأن الوالدة سبب لوجوده فلا يستحق قتلها ولهذا لا يباح له قتل واحد من أبويه وإن كان حربياً أو مرتداً أو زانياً محصناً، فإذا سقط حق ولدها سقط حق الباقي وانقلب الكل مالاً لأن القصاص تعذر استيفاؤه لا لمعنى من جهة القاتل بل حكماً من جهة الشرع فانقلب الكل مالاً بخلاف ما تقدم لأن ثمة العافي أسقط حق نفسه فلا ينقلب نصيبه مالاً.
Book of Claims, Chapter on the Claim of Two Men. He bequeathed. And according to them (Sahibayn) it is in thirds: two-thirds for the one claiming all, one-third for the one claiming half. Second: if he bequeathed all his property to a man and half to another, and the heirs approved, according to Abu Hanifa the property is between them in fourths, according to them in thirds. Third: if he bequeathed a specific slave to a man and half of him to another, and it exits from a third or not, and the heirs approved, the slave is between them in fourths according to Abu Hanifa and in thirds according to them. As for what is divided by way of 'awl according to Abu Hanifa and by way of munaza'a according to them, there are five issues: among them what is mentioned in the chapter on the authorized slave: a slave jointly owned by two men, one of the masters gave him credit (i.e., sold something on credit), and a stranger gave him credit of one hundred, then the slave was sold for one hundred. According to Abu Hanifa, the price of the slave is divided between the creditor master and the stranger into thirds: two-thirds to the stranger, one-third to the master, because his credit is valid in the share of his partner, not in his own share. Second: if a stranger gave him credit of one hundred and another stranger gave him credit of fifty, and the slave is sold, according to Abu Hanifa the price is divided between them into thirds, according to them into fourths. Third: a slave killed a man by mistake and another intentionally, and the intentionally killed has two guardians, and one of them pardons; the slave's master is given the choice between handing over the slave and paying ransom. Then this master ransoms for fifteen thousand: five thousand to his pardoning partner and ten thousand to the guardian of the mistaken killing. If he hands over, the slave is divided between them into thirds according to Abu Hanifa, according to them into fourths. Fourth: if the perpetrator was a mudabbir and the case is as before, and the master pays the value. Fifth: the case of the book: an umm walad killed her master and a stranger intentionally, and each has two guardians; one guardian of each pardons successively. She works for three-fourths of her value; the silent one among the stranger's guardians has a quarter of the value, and half the value is divided between them by 'awl into thirds according to Abu Hanifa, according to them into fourths by munaza'a. The principle for Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: whenever two rights are established on a common basis at one time, the division is by 'awl; if they are established distinctly or at two different times, the division is by munaza'a. The meaning is that analogy precludes division by 'awl, because the interpretation of 'awl is that each of them strikes with all his right: one with half the property and the other with all, and a single property cannot have all and half of another. For this reason Ibn Abbas said: 'Whoever wishes, I will imprecate him: Allah has not made in one property two-thirds and a half, nor two halves and a third.' We only abandoned analogy in inheritance by consensus of the Companions, so what is in its meaning is annexed to it. In inheritance, the rights of all are established on a common basis at one time, which is the state of death. In the estate, if disparate rights come together, like the rights of creditors, they are established at one time, the state of death or illness, so it is in the meaning of inheritance; similarly in bequests. In the case of the slave and mudabbir, if he gouges out someone's eye and kills another by mistake, the right of the injury claimants is established at one time, which is the time of handing over the slave for the injury or the value of the mudabbir, because the obligation for a mistaken injury is not owned before payment; hence zakat is not obligatory on it before receipt, nor is guaranty valid with it; it is only owned at delivery, and the time of delivery is one. In the case of claiming a house, the right is only established by judgment, and the time of judgment is one, so it is in the meaning of the inheritance case. In the sale by a fuduli, the time of establishment of the two rights is different, because ownership is established at ratification retroactive to the time of the contract, and the time of the contract is different. In the fourth category, the time of establishment of the two rights is different: in the credit case, because the right is established by the credit, and the time of credit is different. In the slave who kills one man intentionally and another by mistake, and the intentionally killed has two guardians, one pardons, and the master chooses to hand over the slave, or if the perpetrator was a mudabbir and the case is as before and the master pays the value, according to them it is divided by munaza'a because the time of establishment of the two rights is different: the right of the silent one among the blood guardians was in retaliation because it is a like, and the property is a substitute for retaliation, and the obligation of the substitute is attached to the original cause which is killing, so the time of establishment of his right is the killing; and the right of the guardian of the mistaken killing is in the value, since the handed-over slave is established at the time of handing over, not before, because it is a meaning-gift, and gifts are not owned before receipt; so the time of the two rights is different, so it is not in the meaning of inheritance, and the division is by munaza'a. In the injury of the umm walad, the obligation of blood money for the one who did not pardon is attached to the killing as we said, and the two killings occurred at two different times, so the division is by munaza'a according to them. The principle for Abu Hanifa: division of a specific property when it is by a right established in the dhimma or by a right established in the property on a common basis in a part without the whole, the division is by 'awl; and whenever division of a specific property is obligated by a right established distinctly, or one of the two rights is in a common part and the other in the whole, the division is by munaza'a. The meaning: when rights are established in the dhimma, they are equal in strength because the dhimma is expansive, so each of them strikes with all against the property. Similarly, if each has a right in the property but in the common portion, they are equal in strength, because no part in which one's right is established except that the other can compete with him in it, so the rights are equal in strength. The origin of 'awl is inheritance as they both said, and there the right of each of them is established in a common part. If the two rights are established distinctly, it is not in the meaning of inheritance. Similarly, if one has a right in a common part and the other in the whole, it is not in the meaning of inheritance, because the owner of the whole competes with the owner of the part in everything, but the owner of the part does not compete with the owner in the whole, so it is not in the meaning of inheritance. And because when the right of each is in a common part, and what each takes by the division is not separated and is non-common, the taken is a substitute for his right, not the original right itself, so it is in the meaning of inheritance and the estate in which debts are collected. In the issues of division, obligation is by a right established in the dhimma, because the right of each is in the obligation arising from injury, and the obligation arising from injury is in the dhimma, so the division there is by 'awl. On this basis the issues are derived. This applies if she has no child from the master; if she has a child from the master who inherits him, then there is no retaliation upon her for the master's blood, because the child does not deserve retaliation against his parents; hence if a woman kills her child, retaliation is not obligatory upon her, because the mother is a cause of his existence, so her killing is not deserved; therefore it is not permissible for him to kill any of his parents even if they are a harbi, apostate, or muhsan adulterer. If her child's right falls, the right of the remaining one also falls, and the whole turns into property because the retaliation became impossible to exact not due to a cause from the killer but legally from the Shari'a, so the whole turns into property, unlike what preceded because there the pardoner dropped his own right, so his share does not turn into property.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the principles governing the division of property among multiple claimants, particularly when their claims are of different magnitudes. It is a key intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the underlying legal reasoning (ta'lil) for each position across five specific scenarios. The core disagreement is whether division should be by 'awl (proportional reduction, as in inheritance) or by munaza'a (distribution based on litigation, where each claimant takes a distinct portion). Abu Hanifa generally favors 'awl when the rights are established in the dhimma (liability) or in the property on a common basis, while the Sahibayn distinguish based on whether the rights are established simultaneously and shared. The passage carefully applies these principles to cases of bequests, jointly-owned slaves, debts, and injuries, culminating in the rule for an umm walad who kills her master. The commentary emphasizes that the choice of method affects the shares each claimant receives, and the reasoning relies on analogy to inheritance, consensus of the Companions, and the nature of the right (whether it is a debt or a right in the specific property). The text also clarifies that when rights are established at different times or in distinct portions, munaza'a applies, as seen in the case of a fuduli sale or the killing of two people at different times.

Key Terms
عول ('awl): Proportional reduction of shares when the total of prescribed shares exceeds the estate, as used in inheritance and analogized to other divisions.
منازعة (munaza'a): Division by litigation or contest, where each claimant takes a distinct portion of the property based on the strength of their specific claim, not by proportional reduction.
ذمة (dhimma): The legal capacity or liability of a person, which can hold obligations (debts) and is considered expansive, allowing multiple claimants to have rights against it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, when is division by 'awl (proportional reduction) applicable?
A) Whenever the rights are established in the dhimma.
B) Only when rights are established simultaneously on a common basis.
C) Whenever a single property is claimed by two people.
D) Whenever the claims arise from inheritance or bequests.

Key Takeaway
The choice between 'awl and munaza'a depends on whether the rights are in the dhimma or common part (Abu Hanifa) or whether they are simultaneous and common (Sahibayn).
