Division of a House Among Multiple Claimants: Dispute Between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Explaining the ruling when a house is in the hands of two or three claimants with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on division of jointly possessed property among multiple claimants and distinguish between Abu Hanifa's conflict-based division and the Sahibayn's 'awl method.

Core Idea
When claimants have proof on shared property, Abu Hanifa divides by strength of claim; Sahibayn use proportional 'awl.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a classic scenario: a house is in the hands of two or three claimants, each with evidence. The ruling depends on whether the possessions overlap. Abu Hanifa and his two students differ on the method of division. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply principles of possession, presumption, and evidence in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine the number of claimants and their claims. For two: one claims all, another claims half. For three: one claims all, another two-thirds, another half.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa gives the claimant a choice (or uses conflict-based division for three). The one claiming all gets the entire house from the two-claimant case.
For three, he divides by degree of conflict.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad reject choice and apply 'awl (proportional reduction) to divide the property among all claimants.
4
Analyse the reasoning
Note the presumption that Muslims' affairs are sound (حمل أمور المسلمين على الصحة). The claim is directed to what is in the claimant's hand. So the half in the hand of the one claiming half is not disputed, and goes to the other. The outsider's evidence prevails over the possessor for the disputed half.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
With two claimants: the whole house goes to the one claiming all. With three: Abu Hanifa gives more to the one claiming all; Sahibayn distribute proportionally like inheritance 'awl.
The correct view (الصحيح) is that the claimant may choose according to all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن يصح النصف حنيفة يتخير، وعندهما لا يتخير، والصحيح أن هنا يتخير عند الكل، سواء كان الدفع بقضاء أو بغير قضاء لأن قضاء القاضي يدفع الكل إلى ورثة المولى بعد تعلق حق الأجنبي وثبوته لا يصح بخلاف الوصي إذا قضى دين أحد الغريمين بأمر القاضي حيث لا يضمن لأن للقاضي يضع مال الميت حيث شاء، أما هنا بخلافه، وإذا لم يصح قضاء القاضي هنا لأن لا فعلها بغير قضاء أولى قوله : ولو كانت في أيديهما فهي للثاني أي فالدار كلها لصاحب الجميع نصفها على وجه القضاء ونصفها لا على وجه القضاء لأن دعوى مدعي منصرفة إلى ما في يده لتكون يده يداً محقة في حقه لأن حمل أمور المسلمين على الصحة واجب، فمدعي النصف لا يدعي شيئاً مما في يد صاحب الجميع فيسلم النصف لمدعي الجميع بلا منازعة فبقي ما في يده لا على وجه القضاء إذ لا قضاء بدون الدعوى واجتمع بينة الخارج وذي اليد فيما في يد صاحب النصف فتقدم بينة الخارج، ولو كانت في يد ثلاثة فادعي أحدهم كلها وآخر ثلثيها وآخر نصفها وبرهنوا فهي مقسومة عنده بطريق المنازعة وعندهما بالعول وبيانه في الكافي والله أعلم.
That half is valid. Abu Hanifa says the claimant may choose, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he may not choose. The correct view is that here he may choose according to all, whether the payment is by judgment or without judgment, because the judge's judgment pays the whole to the heirs of the master after the right of the stranger is attached and established, it is not valid, unlike the executor when he pays the debt of one of the two creditors by the order of the judge, where he is not liable, because the judge may place the property of the deceased wherever he wishes. But here it is otherwise. And if the judge's judgment is not valid here, then doing it without judgment is more appropriate. His saying: 'If it is in the hands of both, then it is for the second' means that the entire house belongs to the owner of all, half by judgment and half not by judgment, because the claim of the claimant is directed to what is in his hand so that his hand becomes a rightful hand in his favor, because it is obligatory to assume that the affairs of Muslims are correct. So the claimant of half does not claim anything that is in the hand of the owner of all, so half is handed over to the claimant of all without dispute. What remains in his hand is not by judgment, since there is no judgment without a claim. The evidence of the outsider and the possessor conflict regarding what is in the hand of the owner of half, so the evidence of the outsider is preferred. If it is in the hands of three, one claims all, another claims two-thirds, and another claims half, and they provide evidence, then according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is divided by the method of conflict, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is divided by 'awl (proportional reduction). Its explanation is in al-Kafi. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning a house in the hands of two or three claimants. The ruling is that when two claimants each possess part of the house, the one claiming all gets the entire house: half by judicial decree and half without decree, because the other claimant did not claim that half. When three claimants are involved, Abu Hanifa divides the house by proportional allocation based on degree of conflict (the one with the strongest claim gets more), while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) use the principle of 'awl (proportional reduction) as in inheritance. The correct view is that Abu Hanifa's position giving the claimant a choice is upheld in this context. The reasoning involves the presumption that Muslims' affairs are sound, and the judge's authority to allocate property. The passage also references a distinction from the case of an executor paying one of two creditors by court order, where the executor is not liable because the judge may decide where to place the deceased's property. The explanation is elaborated in al-Kafi.

Key Terms
العول (al-'awl): Proportional reduction of shares when total exceeds the fund; used here metaphorically for division among claimants
يد محقة (yad muhiqqa): A hand that is legally rightful; possession presumed correct in favor of the possessor until proven otherwise
المنازعة (al-munaza'a): Conflict-based division; each claimant gets a share based on the strength of their claim

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a house is in the hands of two claimants—one claiming all and one claiming half—what is the ruling?
A) The house is divided equally between them.
B) The entire house goes to the one claiming all.
C) Each keeps what is in his hand, and the half in dispute is divided.
D) The house is sold and the proceeds divided by 'awl.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when multiple claimants have evidence on a shared property, Abu Hanifa's method (the mufta bihi) gives the entire property to the one claiming all in a two-claimant scenario, and divides by conflict in a three-claimant scenario, while the Sahibayn apply proportional 'awl.

Rulings on Claims of Parentage and Consequences of Sale/Emancipation
A series of case rulings on establishing parentage and consequences of sale and emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on five specific scenarios involving claims of parentage, sale, and emancipation, and apply them to new cases.

Core Idea
A child's free status from paternity can nullify a subsequent sale and emancipation.

This lesson presents a set of decisive Hanafi rulings on complex cases where claims of parentage interact with sale and emancipation. These cases illustrate how the law prioritizes lineage over later transactions and resolves conflicting claims. Understanding these rulings helps you see the legal hierarchy between paternity, ownership, and contractual acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial claim and its legal effect
Consider the first case: a man acknowledges two children as his. The second ruling stops the buyer's emancipation.
The first acknowledgment establishes paternity and free status.
2
Analyze contradictory claims on a child
In the second case, a man first says a boy is another's son, then later claims him as his own. The first claim prevails.
The previous statement creates a binding acknowledgment.
3
Resolve conflict between paternity and ownership
A Christian boy in a Muslim's hand: the Christian claims paternity, the Muslim claims ownership. The boy is free and the Christian's son.
Paternity from a free origin overrides a claim of slavery.
4
Handle joint claims by a married couple
If a married couple each claim a boy from previous relationships, the child is considered the child of both.
Each parent can establish lineage from their side independently.
5
Determine liability when a purchased slave-girl is reclaimed
If a purchased slave-girl gives birth and is later claimed by a third party, the buyer must pay the child's value; the child is free.
The father compensates for the child's value but recovers from the seller.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثبت نسبهما منه، وإن باع أحدهما وأعتقه المشتري بطل عتق المشتري. صبي عند رجل فقال هو ابن فلان ثم قال هو ابني لم يكن ابنه. وإن جحد أن يكون ابنه ولو كان في يد مسلم نصراني فقال النصراني ابني وقال المسلم عبدي فهو حر ابن النصراني وإن كان صبي في يدي زوجين فزعم أنه ابنه من غيرها وزعمت أنه ابنها من غيره فهو ابنهما. ولدت مشتراة فاستحقت غرم الأب قيمة الولد وهو حر، فإن مات الولد لم يضمن الأب قيمته وإن ترك مالاً، وإن قتل الولد غرم الأب قيمته ويرجع بالثمن وقيمته على بائعه لا بالعقر .
His lineage from both is established. If he sells one of them and the buyer emancipates him, the buyer's emancipation is void. A boy with a man: he says 'he is the son of so-and-so' then says 'he is my son' – he is not his son. If he denies that he is his son. If a Muslim has a Christian boy in his hand, and the Christian says 'he is my son' and the Muslim says 'he is my slave', then he is free and the son of the Christian. If a boy is in the hands of a married couple, and the man claims he is his son from another woman, and the woman claims he is her son from another man, then he is the son of both. A purchased slave-girl gives birth and is then claimed (by a third party); the father (the buyer) must pay the value of the child, and the child is free. If the child dies, the father does not guarantee its value, even if it left property. If the child is killed, the father must pay its value, and he recovers the purchase price and its value from the seller, not the dower.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings dealing with claims of parentage and related property issues. The first ruling: if a man acknowledges two children as his, and then sells one of them, the buyer's subsequent emancipation of that child is void because the child's free status (due to paternity) precedes the sale. The second: if a man initially says a boy is someone else's son, then later claims him as his own, the second claim is rejected because it contradicts the first. The third: if a Christian boy is in the hands of a Muslim, and the Christian claims him as his son while the Muslim claims him as his slave, the boy is ruled free and the son of the Christian, because the Christian's claim of paternity takes precedence over the Muslim's claim of ownership, especially since the Muslim's hand is not a rightful hand in this context (the boy was originally free). The fourth: if a married couple each claim a boy as their child from a previous relationship, the boy is considered the child of both (i.e., each can claim parentage from their side, but the child is not necessarily born of their marriage). The fifth: if a purchased slave-girl gives birth, and then the seller is found to have no title (the girl is claimed by a third party), the buyer (father of the child) must pay the value of the child (as compensation to the true owner), and the child becomes free. If the child dies naturally, the father owes nothing even if the child left property. If the child is killed, the father must pay its value, and he can recover from the seller the purchase price and the child's value, but not the dower (since there was no valid marriage).

Key Terms
عقر ('uqr): Dower paid to a woman for intercourse under a void marriage or by mistake; here, the father cannot recover 'uqr from the seller
ثبت (thabata): To be established or proven (lineage)
بطل (batala): To be void; nullified

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man first says a boy is 'the son of so-and-so' and then later says 'he is my son', what is the ruling?
A) The second claim establishes paternity.
B) The first claim is taken, and he is not his son.
C) The boy is declared free and chooses his father.
D) The matter is suspended until investigation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, established paternity takes precedence over later transactions and contradictory claims.

The Definition and Dual Nature of Acknowledgment (Iqrar)
Definition of acknowledgment with its dual nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of iqrar and distinguish between its informative and creative aspects.

Core Idea
Iqrar is both an informative statement and a legal creation: it tells of a right and binds the speaker.

The passage begins the Book of Acknowledgment with a precise definition: iqrar is an informative statement that has a creative effect. Understanding this dual nature is essential to grasp why acknowledgment can apply to future property and why certain conditions must be met.

Guided Path
1
Identify the precise wording of the definition
Find the exact Arabic phrase defining iqrar. Note the two parts: 'إخبار' (informative) and 'إنشاء' (creative).
The text says: 'هو إخبار بحق عليه من وجه إنشاء من وجه'.
2
Analyze the first aspect: informative (khabar)
What does it inform about? A right due upon the speaker. This reports a pre-existing obligation.
It is a report (khabar) of a prior right.
3
Analyze the second aspect: creative (insha')
How is it creative? It creates a legal obligation on the speaker to fulfill the acknowledged right. This makes it binding.
Even if the right is not currently owed, the acknowledgment creates the duty.
4
See the practical implication
The text gives an example: acknowledging property of another that the speaker does not currently own is valid; the speaker must deliver if he later acquires it.
This shows the creative aspect – the obligation is created now.
5
Contrast with other schools
Some schools treat iqrar purely as testimony. The Hanafi view allows acknowledgment of future property, which is broader.
The dual nature is a distinctive Hanafi contribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإقرار ومال عظيم نصاب وأموال عظام ثلاثة نصب ودراهم كثيرة عشرة ودراهم ثلاثة كتاب الإقرار (هو إخبار) بحق عليه من وجه إنشاء من وجه فللأول يصح إقراره بمملوك للغير ويلزمه تسليمه إذا ملكه ولو أقر بالطلاق والعتاق مكرهاً لا يصح، ولو أقر المريض بجميع ماله الأجنبي يصح ولا يتوقف على إجازة الوارث. وصح إقرار المأذون بعين في يده والمسلم بخمر، وصح الإقرار بنصف داره مشاعاً، وإقرار المريض بالزوجية من غير شهود ولا تسمع دعواه عليه بأنه أقر له بشيء معين من غير أن يقول وهو ملكي. ولو علم المقر له أنه كاذب في إقراره لا يجوز له أخذه منه جبراً ديانة كإقراره لأمرأته بجميع ما في منزله وليس لها عليه شيء، وإذا أقر بالمدعى به ثم أنكر إقراره لا يحلف على إقراره بل على المال. والثاني لو رد إقراره ثم قبل لا يصح إلا إذا أضافه إلى غيره متصلاً بالرد كان له، وكذا الملك الثابت بالإقرار لا يظهر في حق الزائد المستهلكة فلا يملكها المقر له وشرطه التكليف والطوع مطلقاً والحرية للتنفيذ للحال لا مطلقا فصح إقرار العبد للحال فيما لا تهمة فيه كالحدود كتاب الإقرار هو إخبار عن ثبوت حق للغير على نفسه إذا أقر حر مكلف بحق صح ولو مجهولاً كشيء وحق ويجبر على بيانه ويبين ماله قيمة والقول للمقر مع يمينه إن ادعى المقر له أكثر منه وفي مال لم يصدق في أقل من درهم قوله : ( وبيانه في الكافي) قال الرملي : ينظر المجمع هنا والتلخيص من البيوع من باب اختلاف البينات فإن هنا بياضاً نحو أربعة أسطر .اهـ. قلت قد سقط من هنا كلام كثير ليس بمقدار هذا البياض فإن المؤلف قد أسقط الكلام على تتمة هذا الباب وأسقط أيضاً الكلام على الباب الذي يليه بتمامه وهو باب دعوى النسب كتاب الإقرار . قوله : (لا يظهر في حق الزوائد المستهلكة يفيد بظاهره أنه يظهر في حق الزوائد الغير المستهلكة وهو مخالف لما في الخانية : رجل في يده جارية وولدها أقر أن الجارية لفلان لا يدخل فيه الولد، ولو أقام بينة على جارية أنها له يستحق أولادها .اهـ والفرق أنه بالبينة يستحقها من الأصل
Book of Acknowledgment. And great wealth is one nisab, and great wealths are three nisabs, and many dirhams are ten, and dirhams are three. Book of Acknowledgment: It is an informative statement of a right due, in one respect it is a creative act. Due to the first, his acknowledgment of property owned by another is valid and he must deliver it if he owns it. If he acknowledges divorce or emancipation under duress, it is not valid. If a sick person acknowledges all his property to a stranger, it is valid and does not depend on the heir's permission. Valid is the acknowledgment of a permitted slave regarding a specific item in his hand, and a Muslim regarding wine. Valid is the acknowledgment of half of his house as shared. The sick person's acknowledgment of marriage without witnesses, and his claim against him is not heard that he acknowledged a specific thing to him without saying 'and it is my property'. If the acknowledgee knows that the acknowledger is lying in his acknowledgment, it is not permissible for him to take it from him by force, as a matter of religious duty, like his acknowledgment to his wife of everything in his house while she has no claim on him. If he acknowledges the claimed thing then denies his acknowledgment, he is not sworn on his acknowledgment but on the property. The second: if he rejects his acknowledgment and then accepts, it is not valid unless he adds it to another, connected to the rejection, then it is his. Similarly, property established by acknowledgment does not appear in the right of consumed excess, so the acknowledgee does not own it. Its conditions are legal capacity and free will absolutely, and freedom for execution immediately, not absolutely. So the acknowledgment of a slave is valid immediately in matters where there is no suspicion, like hudud punishments. Book of Acknowledgment: It is an informative statement about the establishment of a right of another upon himself. If a free, legally capable person acknowledges a right, it is valid even if unknown, like 'something' or 'a right', and he is compelled to explain it and specify its value. The statement of the acknowledger is accepted with his oath if the acknowledgee claims more than that. In property, he is not believed for less than a dirham. His saying: (and its explanation is in al-Kafi). Al-Ramli said: Check al-Majma' here and al-Talkhis from the book of sales, chapter of conflicting evidence, for here there is a blank of about four lines. End. I said: A lot of speech has fallen from here, not of the amount of this blank, for the author omitted the discussion on the remainder of this chapter and also omitted the entire following chapter, which is the chapter on claiming lineage. Book of Acknowledgment. His saying: (does not appear in the right of consumed excess) indicates by its apparent meaning that it appears in the right of non-consumed excess, and this contradicts what is in al-Khaniyyah: A man has in his hand a slave-girl and her child; he acknowledges that the slave-girl is for so-and-so; the child is not included. If he provides evidence that the slave-girl is his, he is entitled to her children. End. The difference is that by evidence he is entitled from the origin.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the Book of Acknowledgment (Kitab al-Iqrar). It defines iqrar as an informative statement that also has a creative aspect: it informs of a pre-existing right but also creates a legal obligation. The passage lists numerous rulings: (1) A person can acknowledge ownership of something for another even if he does not currently own it, but must deliver it if he later acquires it. (2) Acknowledgment of divorce or emancipation under duress is invalid. (3) A sick person's acknowledgment to a stranger is valid and does not require heirs' permission. (4) A slave with permission to trade can acknowledge a specific item in his hand. (5) A Muslim can acknowledge wine (though it is impure, the acknowledgment is valid from a property perspective). (6) Acknowledgment of half a house as shared is valid. (7) A sick person's acknowledgment of marriage without witnesses is valid. (8) If the acknowledgee knows the acknowledgment is false, he must not take it as a religious duty. (9) If one acknowledges a claim then denies, he is not sworn on the acknowledgment but on the underlying property. (10) Rejecting an acknowledgment then accepting it later is invalid unless the acceptance is connected to a new reference. (11) Property established by acknowledgment does not extend to consumed excess (e.g., if the acknowledged item has been used up, the acknowledgee does not get compensation). (12) Conditions for valid acknowledgment: legal capacity (adulthood, sanity), free will, and freedom (but for immediate effect, not absolutely – a slave's acknowledgment may be valid immediately in matters like hudud where no suspicion of collusion). The passage continues with a discussion of unknown acknowledgments and a textual note from al-Ramli about a missing passage. Finally, a critical note on the phrase 'does not appear in the right of consumed excess' – a contradiction with al-Khaniyyah is resolved by distinguishing between acknowledgment and evidence.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): A legal statement informing of a right due upon oneself, with a creative effect (إنشاء), so it is both informative and binding.
المقر له (al-muqarr lahu): The person in whose favor the acknowledgment is made; the acknowledgee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, what does the 'creative aspect' (insha') of iqrar allow?
A) The acknowledgment can only be about existing property.
B) The acknowledgment can create a binding obligation even for property not yet owned.
C) The acknowledgment is invalid if the property is not owned at the time.
D) The acknowledgment is a form of sale.

Key Takeaway
Iqrar in Hanafi law is both informative and creative: it reports a right and binds the acknowledger to fulfill it, even if the property is not yet owned.

Conditions and Key Rulings of Valid Acknowledgment
Series of rulings on validity, conditions, and effects of acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a valid acknowledgment and apply the ruling to specific cases such as acknowledgment under duress, by a sick person, or of wine.

Core Idea
A valid acknowledgment requires capacity and free will; it is binding even for unknown rights, but does not extend to consumed excess.

After defining iqrar, the passage presents a series of rulings that illustrate its scope and limitations. It covers invalidating factors like duress, special cases like the sick person's acknowledgment, and the crucial principle that acknowledgment does not give right to consumed excess (like offspring that have been sold or consumed).

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions of iqrar
The passage states: 'its conditions are legal capacity and free will absolutely, and freedom for execution immediately, not absolutely.' List these three conditions.
Legal capacity (taklif) means being adult and sane. Free will (taw') means no duress. Freedom (hurriyyah) is required for immediate enforcement.
2
Examine each specific ruling
Go through the rulings: (a) duress invalidates, (b) sick person's acknowledgment to stranger is valid, (c) slave with permission can acknowledge, (d) Muslim's acknowledgment of wine valid, (e) acknowledgment of half a house shared valid, (f) acknowledgment of marriage without witnesses valid.
Each ruling illustrates a condition or an exception.
3
Analyze the rule on consumed excess
The acknowledgment does not give right to consumed excess. Understand the difference with evidence (beyyinah) where offspring are included.
The passage contrasts iqrar and evidence: evidence gives ownership from the origin, so offspring are included; iqrar only gives the specific item.
4
Note the nuance on rejection and acceptance
If the acknowledgee rejects then accepts, it is invalid unless connected to the acknowledgment.
This prevents the acknowledgee from picking and choosing.

The Dual Nature of Iqrar: Report and Creation
Definition followed by illustrative rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define iqrar in Hanafi fiqh, distinguish its ikhbar and insha’ aspects, and apply the definition to various scenarios to determine validity.

Core Idea
Iqrar is both a report (ikhbar) of a right and a creation (insha') of an obligation—each aspect governs different rulings.

The Book of Iqrar opens with a definition that captures a unique Hanafi insight: acknowledging a right against oneself is not merely reporting a pre-existing fact; it also creates a new legal obligation. Understanding this dual nature is essential for grasping when an iqrar is valid, when it binds, and when it fails. The passage then applies this definition to a series of concrete cases, revealing its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dual definition
Recognize that iqrar is defined as ikhbar (report) of a right against oneself, from one perspective, and insha’ (creation) from another. The ikhbar aspect relates to reporting a pre-existing right; the insha’ aspect creates a new legal obligation.
This dual nature is unique to the Hanafi school.
2
Identify which aspect controls which ruling
The ikhbar aspect explains why acknowledging another's property is valid and requires delivery when the owner takes possession. The insha’ aspect explains why duress invalidates iqrar for divorce or manumission—such acts require free will to create a new legal effect.
Focus on the reasoning behind each ruling.
3
Apply to special cases
Consider the rulings for a sick person acknowledging to a stranger, an authorized slave's acknowledgment, a Muslim's acknowledgment of wine, and acknowledgment of an undivided share. Each case tests the boundaries of the definition.
Note how the ikhbar aspect allows acknowledgment of wine even though it is not property for Muslims—it is a report of a fact.
4
Note the ethical dimension
If the acknowledgee knows the iqrar is false, he cannot take the property as a matter of religious duty (diyanatan). This shows that iqrar's binding effect does not override truthfulness.
This is a key distinction between legal enforcement (qada’) and religious obligation (diyana).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإقرار
(هو إخبار) بحق عليه من وجه إنشاء من وجه فللأول يصح إقراره بمملوك للغير ويلزمه تسليمه إذا ملكه ولو أقر بالطلاق والعتاق مكرهاً لا يصح، ولو أقر المريض بجميع ماله الأجنبي يصح ولا يتوقف على إجازة الوارث. وصح إقرار المأذون بعين في يده والمسلم بخمر، وصح الإقرار بنصف داره مشاعاً، وإقرار المريض بالزوجية من غير شهود ولا تسمع دعواه عليه بأنه أقر له بشيء معين من غير أن يقول وهو ملكي. ولو علم المقر له أنه كاذب في إقراره لا يجوز له أخذه منه جبراً ديانة كإقراره لأمرأته بجميع ما في منزله وليس لها عليه شيء، وإذا أقر بالمدعى به ثم أنكر إقراره لا يحلف على إقراره بل على المال.
The Book of Iqrar: (It is a report) of a right against him, in one respect, and a creation, in another. Due to the first aspect, his acknowledgment of a owned property belonging to another is valid, and he is obligated to deliver it when he owns it. If he acknowledges divorce or manumission under duress, it is not valid. If a sick person acknowledges all his property to a stranger, it is valid and does not depend on the heir's permission. The acknowledgment of an authorized slave regarding a specific item in his hand is valid, and a Muslim's acknowledgment of wine is valid. Acknowledgment of half of his house as undivided is valid. A sick person's acknowledgment of marriage without witnesses is valid, and his claim against him (the acknowledged) that he acknowledged a specific thing without saying 'it is my property' is not heard. If the acknowledgee knows that he is lying in his acknowledgment, it is not permissible for him to take it from him by force, as a matter of religious duty, like his acknowledgment to his wife of everything in his house while nothing is owed to her. When he acknowledges the claimed property then denies his acknowledgment, he is not sworn about his acknowledgment but about the property.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage begins the Book of Iqrar with a definition. Qiqaar is defined as a report (ikhbar) of a right against oneself, but it also has an element of creation (insha'), meaning that it creates a legal obligation. The commentator then applies this dual nature: due to the report aspect, an acknowledgment of something owned by another is valid and requires delivery when the acknowledgee takes possession. Due to the creation aspect, an acknowledgment under duress for divorce or manumission is invalid because such acts require free will. Several rulings are then stated: a sick person's acknowledgment to a stranger is valid without heir's permission; an authorized slave's acknowledgment of a specific item in his hand is valid; a Muslim's acknowledgment of wine is valid (though wine is not property for Muslims); acknowledgment of an undivided share is valid; a sick person can acknowledge marriage without witnesses. The passage then clarifies that if the acknowledgee knows the acknowledgment is false, it is religiously prohibited for him to take the property. Finally, if a person acknowledges a claim then denies the acknowledgment, he is not sworn about the denial but about the underlying property.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): A report (ikhbar) of a right against oneself, with an element of creation (insha'), binding upon the acknowledgeer.
إخبار (ikhbār): Reporting something; in iqrar, reporting a pre-existing right.
إنشاء (inshā’): Creating a legal consequence directly; in iqrar, the creation of a new obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a sick person acknowledges all his property to a stranger?
A) It is void without heir's permission.
B) It is valid without heir's permission.
C) It depends on the amount.
D) It requires witnesses.

Key Takeaway
Iqrar in Hanafi fiqh is a dual-natured act—both a report and a creation—and its rulings vary based on which aspect is dominant.

Conditions and Scope of Iqrar: Retraction, Capacity, and Vague Acknowledgments
Rulings on retraction, conditions, and vagueness in iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid iqrar (taklif, taw', hurriyah) and apply the rules for retraction, slave iqrar, drunkard iqrar, and vague acknowledgments.

Core Idea
Iqrar requires capacity and free will; vague acknowledgments are valid but must be clarified.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the legal boundaries of iqrar. It addresses retraction, the effect on consumed increases, conditions of the acknowledger (taklif, taw', hurriyah), and the treatment of vague and general expressions. Understanding these rules is essential for distinguishing valid from invalid acknowledgments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on retraction
If a person rejects his acknowledgment then later accepts it, the acceptance is invalid unless he immediately attributes it to another person at the time of rejection.
This preserves the original iqrar as if it was made on behalf of that other person.
2
Examine the effect of iqrar on increases
Ownership established by iqrar does not extend to consumed increases; the acknowledgee only gets the original property. Contrast with bayyinah (evidence) where increases are included.
This distinction is based on the weaker nature of iqrar compared to evidence.
3
Analyze conditions of the acknowledger
Valid iqrar requires taklif (legal capacity), taw' (free will), and hurriyah (freedom) for immediate execution. A slave's iqrar is valid immediately for suspicion-free matters (hudud, qisas) but postponed for suspicious matters. A drunkard's iqrar is valid if drunk by prohibited means (except for hadd of zina and drinking) but invalid if drunk by permissible means.
The condition of hurriyah is only for immediate execution, not for the validity of iqrar itself.
4
Handle vague acknowledgments
An iqrar of something unknown (majhool) is valid, but the acknowledger must clarify it. If he clarifies with a cause that itself involves ignorance (e.g., sale with unspecified object), the iqrar is invalid. If the cause is harmless, he must specify something of value. Ignorance of the acknowledgee or acknowledger can prevent validity if excessive.
The key is whether the vagueness leads to legal harm (gharar fahish).
5
Resolve disputes and apply general expressions
If they dispute whether the property existed at the time of iqrar, the acknowledger's word is taken unless the acknowledgee brings evidence. General expressions like 'all that belongs to me' are valid as iqrar but may be treated as a gift requiring delivery. Specific phrases like 'a great dirham' yield a dirham.
Custom and usage affect interpretation, e.g., 'the right of Islam' is not accepted as a valid interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني لو رد إقراره ثم قبل لا يصح إلا إذا أضافه إلى غيره متصلاً بالرد كان له، وكذا الملك الثابت بالإقرار لا يظهر في حق الزائد المستهلكة فلا يملكها المقر له وشرطه التكليف والطوع مطلقاً والحرية للتنفيذ للحال لا مطلقا فصح إقرار العبد للحال فيما لا تهمة فيه كالحدود والقصاص، ويؤخر ما فيه تهمة إلى ما بعد العتق والمأذون بما كان من التجارة للحال وتأخر بما ليس منها إلى العتق كإقراره بجناية ومهر موطوءة بلا إذن والصبي المأذون كالعبد فيما كان للتجارة لا فيما ليس منها كالكفالة وإقرار السكران بطريق محظور صحيح إلا في حد الزنا وشرب الخمر لا يقبل الرجوع وإن بطريق مباح لا . وصح بالمجهول ولزمه البيان كشيء وحق والقول له مع يمينه في تعيين المجهول وتعيين العبد المغصوب إن كان قائماً وقيمته إن سبباً تضره الجهالة كالبيع والإجارة لا يصح ولا يلزمه شيء، وإن بين ما كان هالكاً، فإن بين سببا لا يضره صح ويبين ما له قيمة فلا يصح في حبة حنطة وصبي حر وزوجة وجلد ميتة. وقوله أردت حق الإسلام في له على حق لا يصدق لأنه خلاف العرف. وجهالة المقر له مانعة من صحته إن تفاحشت كالواحد من الناس على كذا أو لا كلاحد هذين على كذا لا، ولا يجبر على البيان ولكل منهما أن يحلفه . ما وكذا جهالة المقر عليه مانعة نحو لك على أحدنا كذا فلو قيل بعده أهو هذا قال لا لا يجب المال على الآخر وصح بالعام كما في يدي من قليل أو كثير أو عبد أو متاع أو جميع يعرف لي أو جميع ما ينسب لي لفلان وإذا اختلفا في عين أنها كانت موجودة في يده وقت الإقرار أو لا فالقول قول المقر إلا أن يقيم المقر له البينة أنها كانت موجودة في يده وقته. ولو جميع مالي أو ما أملكه لفلان كان هبة لا يجوز إلا بالتسليم ولو قال لفلان على دار أو عبد لا يلزمه شيء أو مال أو مال قليل أو درهم عظيم أو دريهم لزمه درهم (ومال عظيم قال حمر لا ولذا قلنا إن الباعة يتراجعون فيما بينهم بخلاف الإقرار حيث لا يتراجعون
The second: if he rejects his acknowledgment then accepts it, it is not valid unless he attributes it to someone else continuously with the rejection, then it is for him. Similarly, ownership established by acknowledgment does not appear with respect to consumed increases, so the acknowledgee does not own them. Its conditions are: legal capacity and free will absolutely, and freedom for immediate execution, not absolutely. Thus, a slave's acknowledgment is valid immediately in matters where there is no suspicion, like hudud and qisas. Matters with suspicion are postponed until after emancipation. For an authorized slave, regarding commercial matters immediately, and matters not from commerce postponed until emancipation, like his acknowledgment of a crime and the dower of a woman he had intercourse with without permission. An authorized minor is like a slave in commercial matters, not in non-commercial ones like suretyship. A drunk person's acknowledgment in a prohibited manner is valid except in hadd for zina and drinking wine; retraction is not accepted. If in a permissible manner, no. And acknowledgment of something unknown is valid, and he must clarify it, like 'something' or 'a right'. His statement is accepted with his oath in specifying the unknown, and in specifying the usurped slave if it still exists, or its value if it perished. If he specifies a cause that harms him due to ignorance, like sale and lease, his acknowledgment is invalid and nothing is owed. If he specifies a cause that does not harm him, it is valid, and he must specify something of value, so it is not valid for a grain of wheat, a free child, a wife, or the skin of a dead animal. His statement 'I meant the right of Islam' regarding 'he has a right against me' is not accepted because it contradicts customary usage. Ignorance of the acknowledgee prevents validity if excessive, like 'one of the people' for such-and-such; if not like the two above, then no, and he is not compelled to clarify, but each may swear him. Similarly, ignorance of the acknowledging party is a preventer, like 'you owe one of us such-and-such'. If he then says 'is it this one?' and he says no, the property is not owed to the other. And acknowledgment by a general word is valid, as in 'in my hand' of little or much, a slave, a garment, all that belongs to me, or all that is attributed to me for so-and-so. If they differ over whether a specific item existed in his hand at the time of acknowledgment or not, the statement is of the acknowledger unless the acknowledgee provides evidence that it existed in his hand at that time. If [he says] 'all my property' or 'what I own' for so-and-so, it is a gift and is not valid except with delivery. If he says 'so-and-so has a right against me regarding a house or a slave', nothing is owed. Or 'property', 'little property', 'great dirham', or 'small dirham', a dirham is owed. (And great property: [the commentator] said 'red', no. That is why we say that sellers have recourse among themselves, unlike iqrar where they do not have recourse.)
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of iqrar, focusing on retraction and conditions. The first ruling: if a person rejects his own acknowledgment (by saying it is false) and then later accepts it, the retraction is invalid unless he immediately attributes it to someone else at the time of rejection (e.g., saying 'I acknowledged for someone else'). This preserves the validity. Next, ownership established by iqrar does not extend to consumed increases; the acknowledgee only gets the original property. Then the conditions for valid iqrar are stated: legal capacity (taklif), free will (taw'), and freedom (hurriyah) only for immediate execution, not absolutely. This means a slave's iqrar is effective immediately for matters free from suspicion (like hudud and qisas), but matters with suspicion (like debts) are postponed until after emancipation. For an authorized slave (ma'dhun), commercial matters are immediate; non-commercial (like acknowledging a crime) are postponed. An authorized minor is treated like a slave. The drunk person's iqrar: if done in a prohibited manner (by drinking prohibitedly), it is valid except for hadd punishments for zina and drinking (since those require specific conditions); retraction is not accepted. If the drunkard became intoxicated permissibly (by medicine), his iqrar is invalid. Then the passage discusses vague acknowledgments (majhool). Iqrar of something unknown is valid, but the acknowledger must clarify it (like specifying 'something' or 'a right'). His statement is accepted with oath in detailing the unknown or the specific usurped property. If he clarifies with a cause that would harm him due to ignorance (like 'from a sale' where the object is unknown), the iqrar is invalid and nothing is owed. If the cause does not harm him (e.g., a generic debt), it is valid and he must specify something of value. Things without value cannot be subject of iqrar. The statement 'I meant the right of Islam' is unacceptable due to custom. Ignorance of the acknowledgee prevents validity if excessive (e.g., 'one of the people'); if not excessive (e.g., 'one of these two'), it is valid. Ignorance of the acknowledger is also a preventer (e.g., 'one of us owes you'). Then general expressions are valid (e.g., 'all that is in my hand'). If they dispute whether the property existed at time of iqrar, the acknowledger's word is taken unless evidence by acknowledgee. If he says 'all my property for so-and-so', it is a gift requiring delivery. If he says 'so-and-so has a right regarding a house or slave', nothing is owed. Various phrases for amounts are clarified: 'little property' gives nothing? Actually the text says 'or property, or little property, or great dirham, or small dirham' yields a dirham except 'great property'? The text ends with a note that sellers have recourse (in sale disputes) unlike iqrar.

Key Terms
الرجوع (ar-rujū‘): Retraction of an acknowledgment after declaring it false; invalid unless linked to a new attribution.
الجهالة (al-jahālah): Ignorance or vagueness regarding the object or parties of iqrar; can prevent validity if excessive.
التكليف (at-taklīf): Legal capacity (sanity and puberty) required for valid iqrar.
الطوع (aṭ-ṭaw‘): Free will; iqrar must be voluntary.
الحرية للتنفيذ (al-ḥurriyyah li t-tanfīdh): Freedom for immediate execution; a slave's iqrar may be postponed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a drunk person's iqrar valid?
A) Only when drunk by permissible means.
B) Valid if drunk by prohibited means except for hadd of zina and drinking.
C) Always invalid because a drunk person lacks capacity.
D) Valid only for hudud punishments.

Key Takeaway
Iqrar is a binding acknowledgment but its scope is limited by conditions of capacity, free will, and freedom, and vague acknowledgments require specification.

Ruling on Acknowledging the Unknown (al-Iqrar bil Majhul)
Ruling on iqrar bil majhul with comparison to sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on acknowledging an unknown object and explain the obligation of clarification (bayān).

Core Idea
Acknowledging the unknown is valid; clarification is obligatory.

This lesson explores the foundational Hanafi principle that an acknowledgment (iqrar) of an unknown object is valid but requires subsequent clarification. We will see how this differs from sale contracts and what happens when currencies are unspecified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states: 'And acknowledgment of the unknown is valid, and clarification is obligatory.' Recognize that the act is iqrar (acknowledgment) of something unspecified, and the ruling is validity (sahih) with an obligation to clarify.
This ruling applies to the object of acknowledgment (e.g., amount, type).
2
Distinguish iqrar from sale
In the passage, al-Ramli compares iqrar to sale: if someone acknowledges ten red dinars in a country with multiple currencies, it is valid without specifying which type, unlike sale where the most common currency is defaulted. Understand the reason: iqrar's validity with unknown is settled, so clarification is required later; sale requires known price at contract because uncertainty (gharar) invalidates.
The difference stems from the nature of the contract (mutual vs. unilateral).
3
Understand the obligation of bayan
The acknowledger must clarify the unknown element (e.g., specify the amount or type) after the iqrar. If he refuses, the judge can compel him. This ensures the right is delivered.
Bayan is a wajib (obligation) in this context.
4
Apply to a scenario
Example: A says 'I owe you a sum of money' without specifying. According to the ruling, the iqrar is valid, and A must later clarify the exact amount.
The same applies to unspecified items like 'a house' or 'a slave' – but note the special cases later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وصح بالمجهول ولزمه البيان الخ قال الرملي : قدم الشارح في البيع في شرح قوله وإن اختلفت النقود فسد البيع لو أقر بعشرة دنانير حمر وفي البلد نقود مختلفة يصح بلا بيان بخلاف البيع فإنه ينصرف إلى الأروج اهـ. ولا ريب أن معنى قوله لا يصح بلا بيان أي لا يثبت به شيء بلا بيان بخلاف البيع فإنه يثبت الأروج بغير بيان إذ صحة الإقرار بالمجهول مقررة وعليه البيان تأمل. قوله : (لا يصدق لأنه خلاف العرف قيده في التتارخانية بما إذا قال ذلك مفصولاً قال: وإن قال موصولاً يصح قوله : (أو لا قال الرملي : أي إن لم تتفاحش. وذكر الزيلعي قولاً آخر فيما إذا لم تتفاحش ثم نقل عن الكافي أن الصحة أصح فراجعه إن شئت .اهـ وعبارته وبخلاف الجهالة في المقر له سواء تفاحشت أو لا لأن المجهول لا يصلح مستحقاً إذ لا يمكن جبره على البيان من غير تعيين المدعي فلا يفيد فائدته ؛ هكذا ذكر شمس الأئمة وذكر شيخ الإسلام في مبسوطة والناطفي في واقعاته : إن لم تتفاحش جاز لأن صاحب الحق لا يعدو من ذكره وفي مثله يؤمر بالتذكر لأن المقر قد نسي صاحب الحق ولا يجبر على البيان لأنه قد يؤدي إلى إبطال الحق عن المستحق والقاضي نصب لإيصال الحق إلى مستحقه لا لإبطاله اهـ .ملخصاً. وفي غاية البيان عن الواقعات الحسامية أنه يجوز ويحلف لكل واحد منهما إذا ادعى قوله : ( ولو قال لفلان على دار أو عبد لا يلزمه شيء كذا في الأشباه ويخالفه ما في
His statement: (And acknowledgment of the unknown is valid, and clarification is obligatory) etc. Al-Ramli said: The commentator in the chapter of sale in his explanation of his statement 'And if the currencies differ, the sale is invalid' said: If he acknowledged ten red dinars, and in the country there are different currencies, it is valid without clarification, unlike sale where it refers to the most common. There is no doubt that the meaning of 'not valid without clarification' is that nothing is established without clarification, unlike sale where the most common is established without clarification, because the validity of acknowledging the unknown is settled, and clarification is upon him, reflect. His statement: (it is not accepted because it is contrary to custom) was qualified in al-Tatar Khaniyya to when he says it separately. He said: if he says it connected, it is valid. His statement: (or not) al-Ramli said: i.e., if it is not excessive. And al-Zayla'i mentioned another view for when it is not excessive, then he narrated from al-Kafi that validity is more correct, so consult it if you wish. His words: And contrary to ignorance of the acknowledgee, whether excessive or not, because the unknown person cannot be a rightful claimant, since he cannot be compelled to clarify without specification by the plaintiff, so it does not achieve its purpose. Thus mentioned Shams al-A'immah. And Shaykh al-Islam mentioned in his Mabsutah and al-Natifi in his Waqi'at: if not excessive, it is permissible because the right-holder is not beyond mention. In such a case, he is commanded to remember, because the acknowledger may have forgotten the right-holder. He is not compelled to clarify because it may lead to nullifying the right of the rightful claimant, and the judge is appointed to deliver rights to their owners, not to nullify them. Summarized. And in Ghayat al-Bayan from al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyyah that it is permissible and each of them is sworn if he claims. His statement: (And if he says: so-and-so has a house or a slave against me, nothing is owed) as in al-Ashbah. And it contradicts what is in...
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the matn statements about acknowledging the unknown (majhool). The core ruling from the matn is that acknowledging something unknown is valid but clarification is obligatory. The commentator, al-Ramli, clarifies a distinction: if someone acknowledges ten red dinars where different currencies exist, it is valid without specifying which type, unlike in a sale where the most common currency is defaulted. This is because the validity of acknowledging the unknown is established in principle. Then there is a discussion about the phrase 'I meant the right of Islam' – whether it is accepted. The text from al-Tatar Khaniyy distinguishes: if said separately (disconnected from the initial acknowledgment), it is not accepted as it contradicts custom; if said immediately connected, it is valid. Next, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute about ignorance (jahalah) of the acknowledgee. Some scholars (Shams al-A'immah) say it prevents validity whether excessive or not, because an unknown person cannot be a rightful claimant. Others (Shaykh al-Islam, al-Natifi) say if not excessive, it is permissible, as the right-holder is not beyond recall, and the acknowledger may be commanded to remember. The judge's role is to deliver rights, not nullify them. Another view from al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyyah says it is permissible and each claimant can be sworn. Finally, the matn says: if someone says 'so-and-so has a house or a slave against me', nothing is owed because the object is unspecified and not a debt. This is from al-Ashbah, though the text ends with noting a contradiction in another source.

Key Terms
المجهول (al-majhūl): Something unknown in terms of quantity or identity; acknowledging it is valid subject to clarification.
البيان (al-bayān): Clarification of an unknown matter in iqrar; obliges the acknowledger to specify the object or amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on acknowledging an unknown object (e.g., 'I owe you a sum of money')?
A) Invalid, because the object is unspecified.
B) Valid, but clarification is obligatory.
C) Valid, and no clarification needed.
D) Invalid, unless the amount is stated exactly.

Key Takeaway
Acknowledging an unknown object is valid in Hanafi fiqh, but the acknowledger must later clarify the unspecified element.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ignorance of the Acknowledgee (Jahalat al-Muqarr lahu)
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on jahalat al-muqarr lahu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi views on whether ignorance of the acknowledgee invalidates iqrar, and identify the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
Non-excessive ignorance of the acknowledgee does not invalidate iqrar; each claimant can be sworn.

This lesson delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: does ignorance of who is entitled to the acknowledged right invalidate the iqrar? We will see two contrasting positions and the preferred solution.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
The issue is whether jahalat al-muqarr lahu (ignorance of the recipient) prevents the validity of iqrar. The passage discusses two scenarios: excessive (e.g., 'one of the people') and non-excessive (e.g., 'one of these two').
Excessive ignorance is where the pool of potential recipients is too large to be practically identified.
2
Present Shams al-A'immah's view
Shams al-A'immah holds that any ignorance of the acknowledgee, whether excessive or not, invalidates the iqrar. His reasoning: an unknown person cannot be a rightful claimant, and no one can be compelled to clarify without specific plaintiff.
This is a strict view prioritizing certainty.
3
Present Shaykh al-Islam's view
Shaykh al-Islam and al-Natifi hold that if ignorance is not excessive (i.e., the recipient is among a limited, identifiable group), the iqrar is permissible. Their reasoning: the right-holder is not beyond recall; the acknowledger may have forgotten and can be commanded to remember. The judge's role is to deliver rights, not nullify them.
This view allows the iqrar to stand, with a procedure to identify the true recipient.
4
Identify the relied-upon view
The text mentions that al-Zayla'i and al-Kafi consider the view of validity (when not excessive) as more correct (asahh). This is the mufta bihi position.
Tarjih is based on the principle of upholding rights.
5
Explain the practical procedure
According to the relied-upon view, if the ignorance is not excessive (e.g., between two persons), the iqrar is valid. If both persons claim the right, each can be made to swear an oath that the debt is owed to him. This helps identify the true recipient.
Swearing is a method of proof in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وصح بالمجهول ولزمه البيان الخ قال الرملي : قدم الشارح في البيع في شرح قوله وإن اختلفت النقود فسد البيع لو أقر بعشرة دنانير حمر وفي البلد نقود مختلفة يصح بلا بيان بخلاف البيع فإنه ينصرف إلى الأروج اهـ. ولا ريب أن معنى قوله لا يصح بلا بيان أي لا يثبت به شيء بلا بيان بخلاف البيع فإنه يثبت الأروج بغير بيان إذ صحة الإقرار بالمجهول مقررة وعليه البيان تأمل. قوله : (لا يصدق لأنه خلاف العرف قيده في التتارخانية بما إذا قال ذلك مفصولاً قال: وإن قال موصولاً يصح قوله : (أو لا قال الرملي : أي إن لم تتفاحش. وذكر الزيلعي قولاً آخر فيما إذا لم تتفاحش ثم نقل عن الكافي أن الصحة أصح فراجعه إن شئت .اهـ وعبارته وبخلاف الجهالة في المقر له سواء تفاحشت أو لا لأن المجهول لا يصلح مستحقاً إذ لا يمكن جبره على البيان من غير تعيين المدعي فلا يفيد فائدته ؛ هكذا ذكر شمس الأئمة وذكر شيخ الإسلام في مبسوطة والناطفي في واقعاته : إن لم تتفاحش جاز لأن صاحب الحق لا يعدو من ذكره وفي مثله يؤمر بالتذكر لأن المقر قد نسي صاحب الحق ولا يجبر على البيان لأنه قد يؤدي إلى إبطال الحق عن المستحق والقاضي نصب لإيصال الحق إلى مستحقه لا لإبطاله اهـ .ملخصاً. وفي غاية البيان عن الواقعات الحسامية أنه يجوز ويحلف لكل واحد منهما إذا ادعى قوله : ( ولو قال لفلان على دار أو عبد لا يلزمه شيء كذا في الأشباه ويخالفه ما في

Key Terms
جهالة المقر له (jahālat al-muqarr lahu): Ignorance of the identity of the person to whom the acknowledged right is owed.
التفاحش (at-tafāhush): Excessive ignorance, making the identity of the acknowledgee completely unknown (e.g., 'one of the people').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view, what is the ruling if someone acknowledges 'I owe something to one of these two persons'?
A) Invalid due to ignorance.
B) Valid, and each can claim and be sworn.
C) Valid only if both agree.
D) Requires a judge to determine immediately.

Key Takeaway
Non-excessive ignorance of the acknowledgee does not invalidate iqrar; the judge facilitates identification through oaths.

Confession of an Unknown Thing: Validity and Clarification
Explains rulings on confessing vague debts and obligation to specify.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on confession of an unknown thing (majhool) and identify when the confession is valid, invalid, or requires clarification.

Core Idea
Confession of an unknown thing is valid but requires clarification, unless the vagueness is harmful or involves the impossible.

When someone confesses to a debt but the details are unknown, Islamic law does not immediately reject it. Instead, the Hanafi school rules that such a confession is valid in principle, but the confessor must clarify what he owes. This lesson covers the key rulings from the classical text: what makes a vague confession valid, what makes it invalid, and how disputes are resolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
The text begins by stating that confession of an unknown thing is valid, and clarification is obligatory. This is the fundamental principle.
Memorize this: 'Wa saḥḥa bil-majhūl wa lazamahu al-bayān.'
2
Distinguish Harmless vs Harmful Vagueness
If the vagueness does not cause harm (e.g., 'a thing' or 'a right'), the confession is valid. If it causes harm (e.g., in sale or lease where price must be known at contract), it is invalid.
Harm here means the inability to determine rights at the time of contract.
3
Recognize Items Without Legal Value
Some items have no legal value and thus confession to them is invalid: a single grain of wheat, a free child, a wife (as an object), or the skin of a dead animal.
These are examples from the text.
4
Apply Rules on Ignorance of Parties
Excessive ignorance of the beneficiary (e.g., 'one of the people') or the debtor (e.g., 'one of us') invalidates the confession. The confessor is not forced to clarify, but claimants can demand oaths.
This prevents frivolous or coercive confessions.
5
Understand General Confession and Disputes
General confessions like 'all that is in my hand' are valid. If there is a dispute over whether the item existed at the time, the confessor is believed unless the beneficiary proves otherwise. Saying 'all my wealth' is a gift, not a confession.
Gifts require delivery; confessions establish a prior obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح بالمجهول ولزمه البيان كشيء وحق والقول له مع يمينه في تعيين المجهول وتعيين العبد المغصوب إن كان قائماً وقيمته إن سبباً تضره الجهالة كالبيع والإجارة لا يصح ولا يلزمه شيء، وإن بين ما كان هالكاً، فإن بين سببا لا يضره صح ويبين ما له قيمة فلا يصح في حبة حنطة وصبي حر وزوجة وجلد ميتة. وقوله أردت حق الإسلام في له على حق لا يصدق لأنه خلاف العرف. وجهالة المقر له مانعة من صحته إن تفاحشت كالواحد من الناس على كذا أو لا كلاحد هذين على كذا لا، ولا يجبر على البيان ولكل منهما أن يحلفه . وكذا جهالة المقر عليه مانعة نحو لك على أحدنا كذا فلو قيل بعده أهو هذا قال لا لا يجب المال على الآخر وصح بالعام كما في يدي من قليل أو كثير أو عبد أو متاع أو جميع يعرف لي أو جميع ما ينسب لي لفلان وإذا اختلفا في عين أنها كانت موجودة في يده وقت الإقرار أو لا فالقول قول المقر إلا أن يقيم المقر له البينة أنها كانت موجودة في يده وقته. ولو جميع مالي أو ما أملكه لفلان كان هبة لا يجوز إلا بالتسليم ولو قال لفلان على دار أو عبد لا يلزمه شيء
And confession of an unknown thing is valid, and clarification is obligatory, like 'a thing' or 'a right'. And his word with his oath is accepted in specifying the unknown and specifying the usurped slave if it exists and its value if it is lost. If the ignorance causes harm like sale and lease, it is not valid and nothing is incumbent. And if he specifies after it was lost, and he specifies a reason that does not harm, it is valid, and he specifies what has value. So it is not valid for a grain of wheat, a free minor, a wife, or the skin of a dead animal. And if he says 'I meant the right of Islam', he is not believed because it contradicts custom. And ignorance of the person in whose favor the confession is made prevents its validity if excessive, like 'one of the people for such-and-such' or 'like one of these two for such-and-such' — no, and he is not compelled to clarify, but each of them may make him swear. And likewise, ignorance of the person against whom the confession is made prevents, like 'you have such-and-such upon one of us'. If it is said afterward 'it is this one' and he says 'no', then the money is not obligatory upon the other. And general confession is valid, like 'in my hand, from little or much, or a slave, or goods, or all that I know, or all that is attributed to me, for so-and-so'. And if they dispute about the specific item whether it existed in his hand at the time of confession or not, the word is that of the confessor unless the beneficiary provides proof that it existed in his hand at that time. And if [he says] 'all my wealth' or 'what I own is for so-and-so', it is a gift not valid except by delivery. And if he says 'I owe so-and-so a house or a slave', nothing is incumbent upon him.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This is a passage of rulings on confession of vague or unknown matters in Hanafi fiqh. The author states that confessing to an unknown thing (majhool) is valid in itself, but the confessor must clarify what he owes. He is believed with an oath when specifying the unknown quantity or item. If the thing is lost, he specifies its value. However, if the vagueness is harmful (like in sales or leases where price must be known), the confession is invalid. Some items have no value (e.g., a single grain of wheat, a free child, a wife, or an impure skin) and thus confession to them is void. If the confessor says he meant 'the right of Islam' (i.e., zakat), he is not believed because custom understands that as a debt. Ignorance of the beneficiary (muqarr lahu) prevents validity if excessive (e.g., 'one of the people'), and the confessor is not forced to specify, but each claimant can make him swear. Similarly, ignorance of the debtor (muqarr 'alayhi) prevents validity. A general confession (e.g., 'in my hand, little or much') is valid. If there is a dispute over whether the item existed at the time, the confesor's word is accepted unless the beneficiary proves otherwise. Saying 'all my wealth is for so-and-so' is a gift, not a confession, requiring delivery. Saying 'I owe a house or a slave' imposes nothing due to extreme vagueness.

Key Terms
المجهول (al-majhool): The unknown thing confessed; its quantity or quality is unspecified.
المقر له (al-muqarr lahu): The person in whose favor the confession is made; the beneficiary.
المقر عليه (al-muqarr 'alayhi): The person against whom the confession is made; the alleged debtor in a multiple-party confession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'I owe Zayd a house or a slave', what is the Hanafi ruling according to this passage?
A) It is a valid confession and he must specify which one.
B) It is invalid and nothing is owed.
C) He owes the value of a house.
D) He owes a slave only.

Key Takeaway
A confession of an unknown thing is valid in Hanafi law, but the confessor must clarify the details, unless the vagueness is harmful or the item lacks value.

Phrases That Constitute Iqrar (Acknowledgment)
Lists phrases that constitute iqrar and the jest exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which verbal replies constitute iqrar in Hanafi law and state the exception for jest.

Core Idea
Indirect replies like 'weigh it' and 'give me time' are acknowledgments — only mutual jest negates it.

In Hanafi law, an acknowledgment (iqrar) can be established through indirect phrases, not just a direct 'I owe you.' This lesson lists the specific replies that automatically count as iqrar when a debt is claimed, as well as the sole exception: when both parties agree the statement was made in jest. Understanding these phrases is crucial for creditors and debtors to know when a debt is legally recognized.

Guided Path
1
Identify the debtor's reply
When a claimant says 'I owe you a thousand,' the debtor's reply determines whether it is iqrar.
The reply must be one of the listed phrases.
2
Compare with the list of iqrar phrases
Phrases like 'weigh it,' 'count it,' 'give me time,' 'I paid it,' 'I transferred it,' etc., are all iqrar.
The passage lists: اتزنه (weigh it), انتقده (count it), أجلني به (give me time), قضيتكه (I paid it), أحلتك به (I transferred it).
3
Check for the jest exception
If both parties agree that the reply was made jokingly, it is not iqrar.
The exception requires mutual agreement; one party's claim of jest is insufficient.
4
Determine the ruling
If the reply matches a listed phrase and no jest agreement, iqrar is established.
The debtor becomes liable for the debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أمانة قال لي عليك ألف فقال اتزنه أو انتقده أو أجلني به أو قضيتكه أو أحلتك به فهو إقرار وبلا كتابة لا وإن أقر بدين مؤجل وادعى المقر له أنه حال لزمه حالاً وحلف المقر له على الأجل على مائة درهم فهي دراهم مائة وثوب يفسر المائة وكذا مائة وثوبان بخلاف

Book of Acknowledgment. A trust: He said, 'I owe you a thousand,' then (the debtor) said: 'Weigh it,' or 'Count it,' or 'Give me time for it,' or 'I have paid it to you,' or 'I have transferred it to you (for payment)' – it is an acknowledgment. And without writing, it is not. And if he acknowledges a deferred debt and the claimant claims it is due immediately, it becomes due immediately. And the claimant takes an oath regarding the time period. For one hundred dirhams, they are dirhams. One hundred and a garment: he explains the hundred. Likewise, one hundred and two garments – unlike if he combines them, the debt is preferred. (If he said: 'I owe you a thousand' and he said: 'Weigh it,' or 'Count it,' or 'Give me time for it,' or 'I have paid it to you,' or 'I have counted it,' or 'Send tomorrow someone to take it' meaning to receive it or weigh it, or 'First I will weigh it for you today,' or 'Do not take it from me today,' or 'Until it enters my property,' or 'Until my slave returns,' or 'Acquit me of it,' or 'Give it to me as charity,' or 'Grant it to me' claiming that, or 'I have transferred it to you' – it is an acknowledgment, unless they both agree that it was in jest.)

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing various verbal phrases that constitute an acknowledgment (iqrar) in Hanafi law. When a claimant says 'I owe you a thousand,' and the respondent says any of these phrases (like 'weigh it,' 'count it,' etc.), it is considered an acknowledgment of the debt. The exception is if both parties agree that the statement was made jokingly. The passage also covers the case of acknowledging a deferred debt: if the claimant claims it is due immediately, the debtor must pay immediately, and the claimant takes an oath about the term. The example of 'one hundred dirhams and a garment' means the garment explains the hundred (i.e., the debt is 100 dirhams plus a garment worth? Actually it says 'the garment explains the hundred' meaning the hundred is clarified by the garment? The text is dense but the key is that certain phrases are automatically iqrar.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): A voluntary admission by a person of a right or debt owed to another, which is binding and constitutes proof against the declarant.
سخرية (sukhriyya): Jest or mockery; a statement made in jest does not produce legal effects if both parties agree it was jest.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a debtor's indirect reply to a debt claim, such as 'weigh it' or 'give me time,' is an acknowledgment unless both parties agree it was a joke.

What Counts as Acknowledgment: Non-Iqrar Statements
Lists statements that do not constitute iqrar and those that do with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between statements that constitute iqrar and those that do not, applying Hanafi rules to determine the legal effect of equivocal responses.

Core Idea
Not every response is an acknowledgment—the law distinguishes between clear admissions and mere denials or procedural requests.

The Hanafi school sets precise thresholds for what counts as an acknowledgment (iqrar). A simple 'yes' after speech is always binding, but nodding or speaking in passive constructions often is not. This lesson walks through the categories of statements that fail to establish iqrar and the exceptional cases where even a nod suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Iqrar requires an explicit verbal admission without ambiguity. The passage lists statements that are not considered iqrar, such as defensive claims and requests for discharge.
2
Categorize non-iqrar statements
Group the examples: denial-like phrases ('I did not receive'), procedural requests ('discharge me'), and conditional loans ('I only borrowed from you').
3
Distinguish property acknowledgments
Some statements about use (e.g., 'So-and-so resides') are iqrar of a right, but others (e.g., 'he used to reside') are not. Guaranteeing the lessor's due is iqrar of ownership, but guaranteeing the lessee's rent is not.
4
Apply the nod rule
Nodding in response to a question is not iqrar for property, divorce, sale, etc., but is for apostasy/Islam, lineage, and fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبلا كتابة لا) كقوله ما قبضت بغير حق جواباً لدعواه أنه قبض منه بغير حق. وقوله أبرئني عن هذه الدعوى أو صالحني عنها، وقوله ما استقرضت من أحد سواك أو غيرك أو قبلك أو بعدك وقضيتك مائة بعد مائة بعد دعوى المائتين بخلاف دفعت إلى أخيك بأمرك وعليه إثبات ذلك وضمانه للآجر ما يجب له على المستأجر إقرار بملك العين للآجر بخلاف ضمانه للمستأجر مال الإجارة في الإجارة الطويلة لا يكون إقراراً بالملك للآجر بخلاف قوله فلان ساكن هذه الدار فإقرار له بها بخلاف كان يسكنها وفلان زرع هذه الأرض أو غرس هذا الكرم أو بنى هذه الدار وهي في يد القائل مدعياً أنه معين أو مستأجر فليس بإقرار بالعين وكذا هذا الدقيق من طحين فلان بخلاف هذا الطعام من زرع فلان، أو هذا التمر من نخله أو أرضه أو بستانه أو هذا الصوف من غنمه فهو إقرار كقوله قبضت من أرضه عدل ثياب وشراؤه متنقبة إقرار بالملك للبائع كثوب في جراب وكذا الاستيام والاستيداع والاستعارة والاستيهاب والاستئجار ولو من وكيل وكذا قبول الوديعة. وقوله نعم بعد كلام إقرار مطلقاً، والإيماء بالرأس بعد الاستفهام لا يكون إقراراً بمال وعتق وطلاق وبيع ونكاح وإجارة وهبة بخلاف الكفر والإسلام والنسب والفتوى
And without writing, it is not. (Such as) his saying: 'I did not receive it without right' in response to a claim that he received from him without right. And his saying: 'Discharge me from this claim' or 'Settle with me regarding it.' And his saying: 'I did not borrow from anyone except you' or 'other than you' or 'before you' or 'after you' and 'I paid you one hundred after one hundred' after a claim of two hundred – unlike 'I paid to your brother by your order' and he must prove that. And his guarantee to the lessor of what is owed to him by the lessee is an acknowledgment of the lessor's ownership of the property; unlike his guarantee to the lessee of the rental amount in a long lease, it is not an acknowledgment of the lessor's ownership. Unlike his saying: 'So-and-so is a resident of this house' – that is an acknowledgment in his favor; unlike 'he used to reside in it.' And 'So-and-so cultivated this land' or 'planted this vineyard' or 'built this house' while it is in the possession of the speaker, claiming he is a helper or tenant – that is not an acknowledgment of ownership. Likewise, 'This flour is from So-and-so's wheat' – unlike 'This food is from So-and-so's crop,' or 'This date is from his palm tree' or 'his land' or 'his garden' or 'this wool is from his sheep' – that is an acknowledgment, like his saying 'I received from his land a load of garments.' And his purchasing of a veiled woman is an acknowledgment of ownership for the seller, like a garment in a bag. Likewise, pricing, depositing, borrowing, asking for a gift, hiring – even if from an agent. Likewise, accepting a deposit. And his saying 'Yes' after speech is an acknowledgment absolutely. And nodding the head after a question is not an acknowledgment regarding property, emancipation, divorce, sale, marriage, hire, or gift – unlike apostasy, Islam, lineage, and a legal opinion.

Commentary
This passage continues the ruling on what constitutes an acknowledgment (iqrar). It lists statements that are NOT considered iqrar, such as 'I did not receive it unjustly' in response to a claim of wrongful receipt, or 'Acquit me of this claim.' It then provides nuanced examples: guaranteeing the lessor's due is an acknowledgment of the lessor's ownership, but guaranteeing the lessee's rent in a long lease is not. Saying 'So-and-so resides in this house' is acknowledgment of his right to reside, but saying 'he used to reside' is not. Acknowledgment that flour came from someone's wheat is not ownership acknowledgment, but saying dates are from his palm is. Nodding in response to a question is not an acknowledgment for financial or family matters except for apostasy, Islam, lineage, and legal opinion (fatwa).

Key Terms
إيماء بالرأس (ima' bil-ra's): Nodding the head in response to a question, which in Hanafi law is not considered a valid acknowledgment for most matters except specific ones like apostasy or Islam.

Key Takeaway
A statement must be explicit and unambiguous to be an acknowledgment; defensive or procedural responses do not count, and nodding is limited to specific matters.

Ruling on Acknowledging a Deferred Debt When Creditor Claims Immediacy
Ruling on acknowledgment of deferred debt and contrasting case with black dirhams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a deferred debt becomes due immediately upon the creditor's claim and identify when the debtor is still liable despite contradicting the description.

Core Idea
Acknowledging a deferred debt binds the debtor immediately if the creditor claims it is due.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on iqrar (acknowledgment) of deferred debts. In daily transactions, debts may be agreed with a term. If the debtor later acknowledges the debt but the creditor insists it is due immediately, the debtor cannot insist on the term without proof. This rule ensures justice and prevents delaying payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
If a debtor acknowledges a deferred debt and the creditor claims it is due immediately, the debt becomes due immediately (lazima hāl). The debtor's acknowledgment overrides the deferral unless the debtor can prove the term.
The ruling is based on the principle that iqrar is binding and the burden of proving the deferral lies on the debtor.
2
Contrast the black dirhams case
If the debtor acknowledges black dirhams (specific type) but the creditor contradicts the description, the debtor is still liable (yalsamuhu). This is because acknowledgment of the debt itself is sufficient; the description is secondary.
The difference: in the deferred debt case, the term is contested; in the black dirhams case, the debt's existence is not denied.
3
Consider the oath requirement
In both cases, the claimant (creditor) must take an oath. This serves as a safeguard against false claims and is a standard procedure in Hanafi fiqh.
The oath is required in both the deferred debt and black dirhams scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أقر بدين مؤجل وادعى المقر له أنه حال لزمه حالاً كإقراره بعبد في يده أنه لرجل وأنه استأجره منه (ويستحلف المقر له فيهما) بخلاف ما لو أقر بالدراهم السود فكذبه في صفتها يلزمه أما أقر به فقط كإقرار الكفيل بدين مؤجل ولمن عليه دين مؤجل إذا خاف لو اعترف به لا يصدقه إنكار أصل الدين إذا لم يرد توى حقه ومن أقر بعدد مبهم وعطف موزوناً أو مكيلاً كان بياناً له (كمائة ودرهم) أو درهمان أو ثلاثة دراهم فهي دراهم) عطف عليه قيمياً واحداً (لا كمائة وثوب) أو وثوبان وإن متعدداً فبيان (كمائة وثلاثة أثواب ولو قال نصف درهم ودينار وثوب فعليه نصف كل أحد عشر ألفاً فيلزم أن تهدر الواو التي تعتبر مهما أمكن وهنا ممكن فيقال أحد وعشرون ألفاً ومائة وأحد وعشرون درهماً. نعم قوله ولو سدس «الخ) مستقيم أي يقال فيه مائة ألف وأحد وعشرون ألفاً ومائة وأحد وعشرون درهماً لا أنه مستقيم زيادة على العشرة آلاف مائة وثلاثة أثواب
And if he acknowledges a deferred debt and the claimant claims it is due immediately, it becomes due immediately – like his acknowledgment of a slave in his possession that he belongs to a man and that he hired him from him. And the claimant is made to take an oath in both cases. Unlike if he acknowledges black dirhams and then contradicts their description, he is liable. As for acknowledging only that – like the acknowledgment of a guarantor of a deferred debt, and for one upon whom a deferred debt is owed, if he fears that if he admits it, he will not be believed regarding denial of the original debt if he does not want to lose his right. And whoever acknowledges an obscure number and then conjoins a weighed or measured item, it becomes an explanation for it – (like: 'one hundred and a dirham' or 'two dirhams' or 'three dirhams,' they are dirhams) conjoined with one item of value (not like 'one hundred and a garment' or 'two garments,' and if multiple, it is explanation (like 'one hundred and three garments'). And if he says 'half a dirham, a dinar, and a garment,' he is liable for half of each. Eleven thousand: it necessitates dropping the conjunctive 'waw' which is considered whenever possible, and here it is possible, so it is said 'twenty-one thousand and one hundred and twenty-one dirhams.' Yes, his saying 'and a sixth' etc. is straightforward, i.e., it is said 'one hundred thousand and twenty-one thousand and one hundred and twenty-one dirhams,' not that it is straightforward as an increase over ten thousand. One hundred and three garments.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics: first, the ruling on acknowledging a deferred debt – if the creditor claims it is due immediately, the debtor must pay immediately, and the creditor takes an oath. An example is given of acknowledging a slave in one's possession belongs to another and that he hired him from him. Second, the passage deals with ambiguous numerical acknowledgments. When someone acknowledges a sum and then mentions a specific item, the item explains the number. For example, 'one hundred and a dirham' means the total is 101 dirhams (the dirham is added). But 'one hundred and a garment' means the hundred is dirhams and the garment is separate. If multiple items are mentioned, they explain the total. The passage also discusses complex constructions like 'half a dirham, a dinar, and a garment' – he owes half of each. The text includes an example of 'eleven thousand' which requires dropping the 'and' to avoid contradiction, etc.

Key Terms
دين مؤجل (dayn mu'ajjal): A debt with a deferred payment term agreed upon by the parties.
إقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment or confession of a right or debt.
الدراهم السود (al-darāhim al-sūd): Black dirhams, a specific type of coin with a distinct value and description.

Checkpoint
